PHOTO: People wear protective face masks outside at a shopping plaza after New Jersey Governor Phil Murphy said he would sign an executive order requiring people to wear face coverings outdoors to prevent a resurgence of the coronavirus disease (COVID-19), in Edgewater, New Jersey, U.S., July 8, 2020. REUTERS/Mike Segar\" height=\"2464\" width=\"3695\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>People wear protective face masks outside at a shopping plaza in Edgewater New Jersey, on July 8, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The ideal face mask for coronavirus protection blocks large droplets along with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/letter-who-coronavirus-airborne-transmission-precautions-2020-7\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"a1eb32eff9d87288a72875ec4f731c42\">smaller airborne particles</a>.</li>\n<li>In general, masks should have more than one layer and be made of tightly woven fabrics.</li>\n<li>Based on several studies evaluating masks' protection levels, we've ranked the most common types from best (an N95 mask) to worst (masks with a built-in valve or vent).</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>&#160;</p><p>A simple trick can reveal whether your face mask offers sufficient protection: Try blowing out a candle while wearing it. A good mask should prevent you from extinguishing the flame.</p><p>The rule isn't foolproof, but it should help <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-best-face-mask-coronavirus-protection-2020-7\">weed out masks that aren't very protective</a>.</p><p>Ever since the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention began recommending cloth masks for the general public in April, researchers have been evaluating the best materials for filtering the coronavirus. An ideal mask blocks both large respiratory droplets from coughs or sneezes — the primary method by which people pass the virus to others — along with <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/letter-who-coronavirus-airborne-transmission-precautions-2020-7\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"a1eb32eff9d87288a72875ec4f731c42\">smaller airborne particles</a> called aerosols, which are produced when people talk or exhale.</p><p>It should be sealed around the nose and mouth, since any gaps, holes, or vents could allow droplets to leak out and potentially infect another person.</p><p>Assuming masks are worn properly, certain materials consistently perform better than others in studies. Based on the latest research, here's a ranking of the best and worst face coverings:</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f513b59e6ff30001d4e6ef2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mask rankings 03\" height=\"6142\" width=\"5001\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Yuqing Liu/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>'Hybrid' masks are among the safest homemade options</h2><p>As a general rule, mask fabrics should be woven as tightly as possible. That's why fabrics with higher thread counts are better at filtering particles.</p><p>It's also preferable to have more than one layer. The World Health Organizations recommends that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/who-fabric-masks-need-3-layers-to-curb-coronavirus-spread-2020-6\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"2862944a2a3ce27d33e9c8cc00af6f78\">fabric masks have three layers</a>: an inner layer that absorbs, a middle layer that filters, and an outer layer made from a nonabsorbent material like polyester.</p><p>N95 masks are the most protective because they seal tightly around the nose and mouth so that very few viral particles seep in or out. They also contain tangled fibers to filter airborne pathogens — the name refers to their minimum 95% efficiency at filtering aerosols. A recent Duke study showed that <a href=\"https://advances.sciencemag.org/content/early/2020/08/07/sciadv.abd3083\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"a7a59413477e510969337554a31a4548\">less than 0.1% of droplets were transmitted through an N95 mask</a> while the wearer was speaking.</p><p>That's why they're generally reserved for healthcare workers.</p><p>Disposable surgical masks are also made of non-woven fabric. A <a href=\"https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24229526/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"1054a6aade7f3d1d9aba888a0ef208d0\">2013 study</a> found that surgical masks were about three times as effective at blocking influenza aerosols than homemade face masks (that was true, at least, when air flow was slower than a cough but faster than a human breathing during light work).</p><p>Still, there are homemade options that come close to the level of protection of an N95 or surgical mask.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e8b3558c023203777309cb9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Face masks\" height=\"1335\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Packaged surgical face masks.\n<p class=\"copyright\">InkheartX/Shutterstock</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>An <a href=\"https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsnano.0c03252\">April study</a> from the University of Chicago determined that \"hybrid\" masks — combining two layers of 600-thread-count cotton paired with another material like silk, chiffon, or flannel — filter at least 94% of small particles (less than 300 nanometers) and at least 96% of larger particles (bigger than 300 nanometers). Two layers of 600-thread-count cotton offer a similar level of protection against larger particles, but they weren't as effective at filtering aerosols.</p><p>That study, however, conducted measurements at low air-flow rates, so the masks might offer less protection against a cough or sneeze. Still, multiple layers of high-thread-count cotton are preferable to face coverings made from a dishcloth or cotton T-shirt.</p><h2>Fabrics like silk or cotton have more variable performances</h2><p>A&#160;<a href=\"https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7264937/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"287df8a6276358e09231353c64cb34ef\">June study published in the Journal of Hospital Infection</a> found that masks made from vacuum-cleaner bags were among the most effective alternatives to surgical masks, followed by masks made from tea towels, pillowcases, silk, and 100% cotton T-shirts, respectively.&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e82261e2d654f7f673f9536?format=jpeg\" alt=\"sewing masks coronavirus\" height=\"3746\" width=\"5362\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A woman sews hospital masks at the Detroit Sewn facility in Pontiac, Michigan, on March 23, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Rebecca Cook/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Research <a href=\"https://www.medrxiv.org/content/10.1101/2020.04.19.20071779v2\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"290e3d5b2ece755b6e4f2e0cf4f8857a\">from the University of Illinois</a>, meanwhile, found that a brand-new dishcloth was slightly more effective than a used 100% cotton T-shirt at filtering droplets when a person coughs, sneezes, or talks. That study (which is still awaiting peer review) also found that a used shirt made of 100% silk was more effective at filtering high-momentum droplets, likely because silk has electrostatic properties that can help trap smaller viral particles.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acsnano.0c03252\">University of Chicago study</a> came to a different conclusion, however: Those researchers found that a single layer of natural silk filtered just 54% of small particles and 56% of larger particles. By contrast, four layers of natural silk filtered 86% of small particles and 88% of large particles at low air-flow rates.</p><h2>Bandanas and scarves don't offer great protection</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f0de2de4dca6804c8344d43?format=jpeg\" alt=\"bandana face mask\" height=\"1487\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Kevin Houston uses a bandana to cover his face on April 23, 2020, in Evanston, Illinois.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Stacey Wescott/Chicago Tribune/Tribune News Service/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Bandanas and scarves have performed poorly in multiple studies.&#160;</p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7264937/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"287df8a6276358e09231353c64cb34ef\">Journal of Hospital Infection study</a> found that a scarf only reduced a person's infection risk by 44% after they shared a room with an infected person for 30 seconds. After 20 minutes of exposure, the scarf only reduced infection risk by 24%.</p><p>Similarly, the Duke researchers found that bandanas <a href=\"https://advances.sciencemag.org/content/early/2020/08/07/sciadv.abd3083\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"a7a59413477e510969337554a31a4548\">reduced the rate of droplet transmission</a> by a factor of two, which makes them less protective than most other materials.</p><p>For the most part, though, any mask is better than no mask, with one notable exception: The CDC cautions people not to wear masks with built-in valves or vents.</p><p>Masks with one-way valves can expel infectious particles into the atmosphere, helping to fuel transmission.</p><h2>Mask studies should be taken with a grain of salt</h2><p>Although research is coalescing around the idea that a few types of masks offer the best protection, it's not always easy to simulate how a mask will perform in real life.</p><p>That's because only some tests directly mimic the size of novel coronavirus particles, while others evaluate performance based on viruses like influenza. Researchers also still aren't sure about the degree to which the virus gets transmitted via aerosols, since those tiny particles are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/liquid-membrane-traps-coronavirus-particles-airborne-transmission-2020-7\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"bc7b5836f95ed53a2dacc73c10529f2b\">extremely hard to trap</a> and study without killing the virus. Some scientists even have different ideas of what constitutes an aerosol — the generally accepted cutoff is less than 5 microns (that's roughly the size of a dust particle) — and many experts think the delineation is arbitrary altogether.&#160;</p><p>Different studies also test masks under different circumstances: Some mimic the heavy air flow produced when a person coughs, while others mimic the air flow when a person is talking or breathing normally.</p><p>And of course, masks perform differently depending on how they're worn. That's why it's better to stick with more protection over less.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"'I never got cards or gifts with Black people on them': A new marketplace takes on Hallmark and fills a historic gap in the greeting card industry","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/new-marketplace-tackles-the-lack-of-diversity-in-greeting-cards-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5270cce6ff30001d4e72a5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Avila.Diana card\" height=\"1210\" width=\"1614\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Avila.Diana</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Kutenda is an online marketplace platforming cards and gifts designed by artists and entrepeneurs from marginalized groups &#8211; the first business of its kind in the world.</li>\n<li>The marketplace hopes to normalise the portrayal of the LGBTQ+ community, the BAME community, and those who identify as disabled in greeting cards.</li>\n<li>Nearly 60% of people agree that card shops should offer more gender neutral designs, a GlobalData survey shows.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The world's first online marketplace for greeting&#160;cards featuring and designed by diverse and underrepresented communities launched on Saturday to mark Black Pound Day,&#160;a day that encourages spending at Black-owned businesses in the UK.</p><p><a href=\"https://kutenda.co.uk/\">Kutenda</a> aims to normalize the portrayal of marginalized groups in cards and gifts so that they can buy products that accurately represent them. This includes the LGBTQ+ community, the BAME community, and those who identify as disabled. Despite the UK spending around <a href=\"http://www.greetingcardassociation.org.uk/resources/for-publishers/the-market/facts-and-figures\">£1.7 billion</a> ($2.25 billion) annually on greeting cards, <a href=\"https://www.stylist.co.uk/life/greetings-cards-lack-of-diversity-interracial-couples-anniversary-valentines-birthday-cards/272581\">the industry doesn't accurately represent marginalized groups</a>.</p><p>Kutenda also platforms the work of up-and-coming artists and entrepreneurs from diverse backgrounds, saying that \"large retailers either ignore minority artists or steal their ideas.\" Alongside cards, the marketplace also sells gifts including mugs, stationery, and bookmarks.</p><p>Founder Avila Diana Chidume said Kutenda hopes to \"create a sense of belonging in a world created to not adequately provide representation.\" The young entrepreneur named the company after the word for \"thankful\" in Shona, a language spoken in her home country of Zimbabwe.</p><p>Chidume was motivated to create the business by the cards she received growing up. \"I could never relate to, or understand why, I never got cards or gifts with Black people on them,\" she said, adding that the first ever birthday card she got featuring a Black person was for her 21st birthday – and it was one of her own designs from her greeting card company <a href=\"https://aviladiana.com/\">Avila.Diana</a>, which she launched in response to this problem.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5271b9e6ff30001d4e72ab?format=jpeg\" alt=\"avila.diana 2\" height=\"1166\" width=\"1555\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chidume launched her greeting cards line Avila.Diana while studying for her bachelors degree.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Avila.Diana</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Chidume isn't the only person to recognize <a href=\"https://www.stylist.co.uk/life/greetings-cards-lack-of-diversity-interracial-couples-anniversary-valentines-birthday-cards/272581\">this underrepresentation in greeting cards</a>. Nearly 60% of respondents to a <a href=\"https://store.globaldata.com/report/vr0125oc--all-year-gifting-cards-gift-wrap-2019/?utm_source=RetailInsight&utm_medium=Research%20Reports&utm_campaign=RSReportPageportPage\">GlobalData survey</a> in 2019 agreed that card shops should offer more gender neutral designs.</p><p>Other entrepreneurs have also responded to this problem. <a href=\"https://huetribe.com/\">Huetribe</a> was launched in 2017 after its founder struggled to find greeting&#160;cards reflecting her interracial relationship, and donates some of its profits to charities supporting racial, cultural and LGBTQ equality. Since 2005 <a href=\"https://www.theafrocardcompany.com/about\">The Afro Card Company</a> has also been creating greeting cards that represent the Black community.&#160;</p><p>But Kutenda is the first of its kind to act as a marketplace for marginalized artists and entrepreneurs to showcase their products.</p><p>&#160;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5272d97ed0ee001e25d942?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Avila.Diana nurse\" height=\"1155\" width=\"1540\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Black Pound Day aims to encourage spending at Black-owned businesses.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Avila.Diana</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Though the business launched on Saturday, it has also set up a <a href=\"https://www.crowdfunder.co.uk/kutendaofficial\">crowdfunder</a> to raise £10,000 ($13,200) to maintain its website and support the brands selling their products through Kutenda.</p><div SD-03","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/japans-first-public-test-flight-flying-manned-car-sd-03-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f524afde6ff30001d4e714f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"SD 03_Flight2\" height=\"1408\" width=\"1877\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SkyDrive&#39;s SD-03 flying car model.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://en.skydrive2020.com/\" target=\"_blank\">SkyDrive/CARTIVATOR</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Japan-based SkyDrive has completed its first public manned flying car test on Aug. 25.</li>\n<li>The SD-03 successfully cruised around the test field for four minutes with a pilot.</li>\n<li>Three days after the test flight, SkyDrive announced that the company raised around $36.6 million in a Series B round of funding.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The idea of a flying car is no longer as futuristic as it sounds: Japan-based SkyDrive has completed its first public manned flying car test.</p><p>The flying SD-03 demonstration took place on Aug. 25 at the Toyota Test Field in Japan, where SkyDrive develops its products, <a href=\"https://skydrive2020.com/archives/3506\">according to the company's news release</a>. This occasion also serves as the country's first public manned flying car test, which took place two years after SkyDrive was formally launched, and seven years after the start of the flying car development under Cartivator, SkyDrive's founding company and joint developer.</p><p>SkyDrive's <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=58kEzTpPzS0&feature=emb_titleitle\">YouTube</a> debut of the flight demonstration passed the <a href=\"https://skydrive2020.com/archives/3708\">one million view mark</a>&#160;within three days of posting. And three days after the test flight, the company <a href=\"https://skydrive2020.com/archives/3461\">announced on a news release</a> that it had raised around $36.6 million in a Series B round of funding.</p><p>According to the SkyDrive, the goal is to be approved for flights outside of the test field before the end of the year.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tThe SD-03 cruised around the test field for four minutes with a pilot ...\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f524ba37ed0ee001e25d7ea?format=jpeg\" alt=\"SD03_1\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SkyDrive&#39;s SD-03 flying car model.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://en.skydrive2020.com/\" target=\"_blank\">SkyDrive/CARTIVATOR</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\t...  who was accompanying the computer-run controls and the on-site staff who were monitoring in case backup was needed.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f524c17e6ff30001d4e7161?format=jpeg\" alt=\"SD 03_内装1\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SkyDrive&#39;s SD-03 flying car model.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://en.skydrive2020.com/\" target=\"_blank\">SkyDrive/CARTIVATOR</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAs of now, the SD-03 is the world's smallest electric vertical take-off and landing (eVTOL) vehicle at 6.56 feet tall, and 13.12 feet wide and long, according to SkyDrive.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f524bd8e6ff30001d4e715d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"SD03 4\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SkyDrive&#39;s SD-03 flying car model.\n<p parking spots.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f524bf2e6ff30001d4e715f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"SD 03_内装3\" height=\"1666\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>SkyDrive&#39;s SD-03 electric motors that are paired off and located at its four corners.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f524baee6ff30001d4e7158?format=jpeg\" alt=\"SD03 9\" height=\"1178\" 22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"A Belgian company says its the first ever to 3D-print a 2-story house in one piece in a breakthrough for sustainable design — see inside","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/kamp-c-3d-printed-two-story-house-in-belgium-2020-8","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c266a6c6e1f001d604806?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Kamp C 3D printed houe\" height=\"1384\" width=\"1845\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>3D-printed house.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kamp C &#38; Jasmien Smets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>A Belgian company just 3D-printed a two-story house in one piece for the first time.</li><li>It used the largest 3D printer in Europe.&#160;</li><li>The building is a demo and is just under 1,000 square feet.&#160;</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>Kamp C just became the first in the world to <a href=\"https://www.kampc.be/c3po\">3D print a two-story house</a> in one piece, using the largest 3D printer in Europe.</p><p>The house in Westerlo, Belgium, is a demo for this style of 3D printing, showing off different styles. It's also a way to measure how the home, which was built using greener practices than typical constructions, holds up over time.&#160;</p><p>Kamp C's 3D printed house is part of the European C3PO project, supported by the European Regional Development Fund. The project brings together scientists and business people to advance 3D printing in Flanders.&#160;</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tKamp C used a 3D printer to print a two story, 968 square foot house.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c30bdb2fa21001d8da9e4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Kamp C 3D printed houe\" height=\"1356\" width=\"1808\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>3D-printed house.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kamp C &#38; Jasmien Smets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe massive 3D printer is the biggest in all of Europe.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c37a56c6e1f001d60487a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Kamp C 3D printed houe\" height=\"1339\" width=\"1786\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>3D-printed house.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kamp C &#38; Jasmien Smets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe house is two floors, a first and a breakthrough in the world of 3D printed construction.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c37cbb2fa21001d8daa18?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Kamp C 3D printed houe\" height=\"1456\" width=\"1941\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>3D-printed house.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kamp C &#38; Jasmien Smets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\t\"The homes that have already been printed worldwide have only one floor and are often in parts factory printed and assembled on site. We have printed the entire building envelope as a whole on the site,\" project manager Emiel Ascione said.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c3805b2fa21001d8daa1a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Kamp C 3D printed houe\" height=\"1456\" width=\"1941\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>3D-printed house.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kamp C &#38; Jasmien Smets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAs Ascione explained, 3D printed homes do already exist, but the term usually describes individual pieces that are printed and later fitted together.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c384b6c6e1f001d604883?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Kamp C 3D printed houe\" height=\"1332\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>3D-printed house.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kamp C &#38; Jasmien Smets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe house is three times stronger than a regular build, according to Kamp C.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c38bc6c6e1f001d604887?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Kamp C 3D printed houe\" height=\"1061\" width=\"1414\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>3D-printed house.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kamp C &#38; Jasmien Smets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAs the demo house, it was printed over three weeks, but Kamp C predicted that in the future houses could be printed in as little as two days.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c266a6c6e1f001d604806?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Kamp C 3D printed houe\" height=\"1384\" width=\"1845\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>3D-printed house.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Kamp C &#38; Jasmien Smets</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIt was printed with different types of walls to show the possibilities of 3D printing.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c394f6c6e1f001d60488a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Kamp C 3D printed houe\" height=\"2000\" width=\"1322\" actor playing President Barack Obama\n<p class=\"copyright\">YouTube</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Extracts from Michael Cohen's new memoir allege that Trump was consumed by an obsessive hatred for Barack Obama, the US' first Black president.&#160;</li>\n<li>In one bizarre incident, Trump hired an Obama lookalike and \"ritualistically belittled the first black his ex-boss' obsessive hatred of President Barack Obama in extracts from his upcoming memoir published by news outlets Saturday.&#160;</p><p>In an extract of Cohen's \"Disloyalty: A Memoir,\" <a href=\"https://edition.cnn.com/2020/09/05/politics/michael-cohen-book-trump-white-house/index.html\">published by CNN</a> and the <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/cohen-trump-book/2020/09/05/235aa10a-ef96-11ea-ab4e-581edb849379_story.html\">Washington Post,</a> Cohen claims that Trump described Obama as a \"Manchurian candidate\" who owed his place at Columbia University and Harvard Law School to \"f---ing affirmative action.\"</p><p>According to the CNN extract, Trump, in pursuing his grudge against Obama, hired a lookalike \"Fauxbama\" and \"ritualistically belittled the first black president and then fired him\" in a bizarre video.</p><p>In the book, reports CNN, Cohen does not name the man hired to play Obama or say on what date the incident took place, but does include a picture from the video.&#160;</p><p>It shows Trump sitting across his Trump Tower desk from a man resembling Obama. On the desk in front of Trump are two books, one with Obama's name on the front.&#160;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Pervaiz Shallwani  (@Pervaizistan) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1302427987929899008?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">September 6, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>&#160;</p><p>But a copy of the video has emerged online</p><p>A parody of Trump's hit reality show The Apprentice, it was supposed to be aired at the 2013 RNC convention, according to reports, but was canned by party bosses.&#160;</p><p>In the video, <a href=\"https://www.breitbart.com/politics/2013/07/06/exclusive-watch-never-before-seen-full-video-of-donald-trump-firing-obama/\">published by Breitbart in 2013</a>, Trump attacks the Obama lookalike's record as president, his lack of business experience, and his golf game. It ends with Trump hurling his \"you're fired\" Apprentice catchphrase at Obama and banishing him from his office.&#160;</p><p>\"They never put it on,\" Trump told Breitbart of the RNC decision not to air the video at the time. \"The reason they didn't put it on is because they thought it was too controversial. Controversy. It might not be politically correct.\"</p><p>Cohen, in extracts of the book published by the Post, details several racist diatribes by Trump. Cohen claims that when ranting about Obama in one incident, he went on to say, \"tell me one country run by a black person that isn't a s---hole. They are all complete f---ing toilets.\"</p><p>According to the extracts, Trump belittled minority voters, saying, \"I will never get the Hispanic vote. Like the blacks, they're too stupid to vote for Trump.\"</p><p>He also, writes Cohen, insulted South African leader Nelson Mandela, and praised the racist Apartheid regime.&#160;</p><p>\"Mandela f---ed the whole country up. Now it's a s---hole. F--- Mandela. He was no leader,\" Cohen claims Trump said.&#160;</p><p>In the book, Cohen's assessment of his former boss's character is withering, and he describes him as \"a cheat, a liar, a fraud, a bully, a racist, a predator, a con man.\"</p><p>But the White House has hit back at Cohen, who was jailed last year for lying to Congress and for election finance crimes prosecutors claimed were committed at Trump's behest.&#160;</p><p>In a statement to the Post, the White House attacked Cohen's credibility, describing him as \"a disgraced felon and disbarred lawyer, who lied to Congress. He has lost all credibility, and it's unsurprising to see his latest attempt to profit off of lies.\"</p><p>But Cohen is not the first source to have claimed that Trump is consumed by hatred for Obama.&#160;</p><p>Trump launched his political career with the racist \"birther\" conspiracy theory, claiming, groundlessly, that Obama was ineligible for the presidency because he wasn't born in the US. (Obama was born in the US state of Hawaii.)&#160;</p><p>In a notorious incident at the 2011 White House Correspondents Dinner, Obama singled out Trump in the audience and mocked him. Some <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/arts-and-entertainment/wp/2017/02/26/did-the-2011-white-house-correspondents-dinner-spur-trump-to-run-for-president/\">pundits have speculated the public humiliation</a> was a key factor in Trump's decision to run for the presidency in 2016.&#160;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a recommendations","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-outlook-downturn-strategy-stay-invested-3-recommendations-ubs-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cfad0d211e2054007798c37?format=jpeg\" alt=\"trader upset angry sad nyse\" height=\"914\" width=\"1829\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty Images / Drew Angerer</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>The stock market sharply sold off this week just days after the S&#38;P 500 hit a fresh record high and notched its best August performance in 34 years.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong>\"We view the latest sell-off as a bout of profit-taking after a strong run,\" said Mark Haefele, the chief investment officer of global wealth management at UBS, in a Friday note.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong>Haefele said that investors should stay the course according to their previous investment plans, and offered three recommendations for staying in the game amid the recent market downturn.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/\">Read more on Business Insider</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>The stock market's latest selloff shouldn't spark concern or prompt investors to make any sudden changes to their portfolios, according to the world's largest wealth manager.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-index-reaction-august-jobs-report-economy-2020-9-1029563648\">The S&#38;P 500 fell sharply Friday</a> just days after hitting a <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/news/stock-market-news-today-sp500-nasdaq-record-stimulus-expectations-2020-9-1029557908\">fresh record high</a> on the heels of its best <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-sp500-dow-august-returns-tech-rally-2020-8-1029549640\">August performance in 34 years.</a> The Dow Jones industrial average and the Nasdaq also slumped, reversing gains from earlier in the week.&#160;</p><p>\"We view the latest sell-off as a bout of profit-taking after a strong run,\" said Mark Haefele, the chief investment officer of global wealth management at UBS, in a Friday note. \"Stocks are still well-supported by a combination of Fed liquidity, attractive equity risk premiums, and an ongoing recovery as economies reopen from the lockdowns.\"</p><p>While the S&#38;P 500 is now sitting roughly at UBS's target, there's also further upside that could be driven by a coronavirus vaccine or \"positive medical developments,\" a new stimulus bill from the government with an election outcome favorable to growth, and a real rates dropping further, according to the note.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-crash-bofa-september-meltdown-risks-technical-indicators-2020-9\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bank of America lays out the under-the-radar indicators showing that huge swaths of the stock market are 'running on fumes' — and warns a September meltdown may just be getting started</a></em></p><p>Investors should thus stay invested according to previous plans, according to Haefele. Here are three recommendations he has for investors.&#160;</p><p><strong>1. Ease into markets&#160;</strong></p><p>Heightened volatility can be scary, but shouldn't mean investors get stuck on the sidelines. \"Rather than trying to time the market and potentially miss out on gains, we recommend an averaging-in approach by establishing a set schedule to commit capital to stocks within a 12-month timeframe,\" said Haefele.&#160;</p><p>He also recommended a \"put-writing approach to enter markets defensively, for those investors who can implement options,\" and \"making use of structured investments to add asymmetric exposure to stocks, e.g., with a degree of capital protection.\"</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/us-investing-championship-strategy-matthew-caruso-contender-secret-to-return-2020-8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">US Investing Championship hopeful Matthew Caruso landed a 382% return in the first half of 2020. He shares the unique twist he's putting on a classic trading strategy — and 3 stocks he's holding right now.</a></em></p><p><strong>2. Diversify for the next leg&#160;</strong></p><p>\"The mega-cap IT complex has driven an outsize portion of the year-to-date gains in the US equity market,\" Haefele wrote. \"But while we don't think tech is in a bubble, we do recommend that investors with excess exposure to the biggest US stocks consider rebalancing into areas accelerated by COVID-19, such as companies exposed to the 5G rollout, and sustainability-aligned companies set to profit from a 'green recovery.'\"</p><p><strong>3. Protect against the downside&#160;</strong></p><p>\"COVID-19 has brought unprecedented uncertainty for investors, and further volatility cannot be ruled out,\" said Haefele. \"Diversification across asset classes and regions is the best way to manage the risks in one's portfolio.\"</p><p>That being said, Haefele added that investors will need to seek alternatives to portfolio diversification because of how low starting yields are on high-quality bonds. He recommended gold, which he sees as having further upside potential, and \"including some exposure to hedge funds with a strong track record of downside risk management,\" to insulate portfolios.&#160;</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-market-crash-expert-says-hypervalued-market-set-to-plunge-2020-9\" target=\"_blank\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/nIdnniQ3Rzg\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sun, 06 Sep 2020 13:10:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5cfad0c311e2053c903c32da?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"3708fcea104a5b4b535aac011b87eadd","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn80@2020_6/2020/09/06/14-05-27-830_efd6606804aef41d.webp","destWidth":1776,"destHeight":1332,"sourceBytes":107944,"destBytes":107944,"author":"insider@insider.com (Carmen Reinicke)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5cfad0d211e2054007798c37?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn67@2020_6/2020/09/06/14-05-45-762_f8f1596c8d5dfe30.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn76@2020_4/2020/09/06/14-05-49-381_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=nIdnniQ3Rzg:IzaHwcBHHLU:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn43@2020_3/2020/09/06/14-05-45-366_d862ce09c6786a77.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=nIdnniQ3Rzg:IzaHwcBHHLU:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn28@2020_3/2020/09/06/14-05-45-300_f2da15ba258ffea0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn71@2020_5/2020/09/06/14-05-44-327_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=nIdnniQ3Rzg:IzaHwcBHHLU:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn96@2020_6/2020/09/06/14-05-33-778_34184e6f64c1d02b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/nIdnniQ3Rzg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn44@2020_6/2020/09/06/14-05-35-527_b2decce95365b898.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599401096931},{"createdTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"Social media is a parasite, it bleeds you to live","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/delete-social-media-phone-parasite-mental-health-instagram-twitter-facebook-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f4fa9887ed0ee001e25cf5c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"cell phones parents\" height=\"2769\" width=\"5539\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Social media apps are designed using the same psychology as casino slot machines. They entice you with menial rewards to keep you coming back, even when you know it's doing you harm.&#160;</li>\n<li>When I deleted social media apps from my phone, I found myself newly endowed with time, mental bandwidth, and imagination that would have been lost to mindless \"doomscrolling.\"</li>\n<li>You don't need to go cold turkey, just stop giving the parasitic social media sites so much of your lifeblood and get the apps off your phone.&#160;</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>You don't need social media, it needs you.&#160;</p><p>It's a parasite, its life force borne of your confessions, photos, memes, and soon-to-be-mortifying opinions. Perversely, it convinces you that feeding the social media beast&#160; is essential to your mental health and career by making you feel \"connected.\"&#160;&#160;</p><p>Twitter, Facebook, Instagram, and the rest, aren't inherently evil websites. But they all operate as sociopaths would: always in their own interests, without conscience, at the expense of others.&#160;</p><p>They entice with promises of&#160; validation and reward. Your work is shared widely. Your cause is amplified. You get a dopamine fix from positive reactions, or even any reactions.&#160;</p><p>They're the online cousins of casino slot machines. They're even <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/technology/2018/may/08/social-media-copies-gambling-methods-to-create-psychological-cravings\">designed using the same psychology</a>, where profits are maximized by actively enabling addiction.&#160;</p><p>And the only rule of casinos is that sooner or later, the house always wins.&#160;</p><h2>If you don't want to delete your account, at least delete the app</h2><p>Earlier this summer, I found my mental capacity was stretched thin. I'm hardly alone in this time of pandemic and social upheaval.&#160;</p><p>I've known for years that social media was a time suck. But lately, more than ever, I could feel myself growing anxious just a couple minutes into mindless \"<a href=\"https://www.wired.com/story/stop-doomscrolling/\">doomscrolling</a>\"&#160;</p><p>For all the personal and professional connections made, the worthwhile articles read, and the occasional laugh, it became evident that social media was not giving me anything close to the emotional value of what I was putting into it.&#160;</p><p>It was swallowing my time, which as a parent of three young kids, is spare. It was scrambling my once-decent attention span. And it was convincing me to care deeply about all kinds of ephemeral internet mush — things not worth caring about at all.&#160;</p><p>Even Instagram, generally a source of hi-fives for my cute kids' photos, started feeling toxic. Underneath the \"living your best life\" facade lurked a cycle of what I call \"envy porn\" — basically content meant to instill the most <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fear_of_missing_out\">FOMO</a> on a global scale. Even if its users (a.k.a. content creators) mean well, Instagram is a place for people — <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/11/02/opinion/sunday/instagram-social-media.html\">especially women</a> — to feel worse about themselves.&#160;</p><p>One afternoon, while eating lunch and scrolling down a Twitter rabbit hole of QAnon content, I rashly decided to delete all social media apps from my phone. I didn't delete my accounts, I just made a de facto rule: no social media on the phone.&#160;</p><p>It's been over two months, my life is better for it.&#160;</p><p>To be sure, I didn't totally go cold turkey. Twitter still hums on my desktop, for work, of course. Popping in on the latest journalistic flame wars, the ritualistic dunkings, and the rare but appreciated article worth reading maintains the \"connection,\" but it no longer feels like a limb.&#160;</p><p>There's been more book-reading, more music-listening, more goofing around with my kids. During all those simple but life-affirming experiences, a portion of my brain doesn't feel permanently tethered to the online matrix. I didn't even have to make a big show of \"leaving social media.\" All it took was getting social media off my phone.&#160;</p><p>Nobody is so thirsty for digital hearts that they're going to walk around mindlessly scrolling on a laptop. And yet, vacantly staring at hot takes and shitposts is socially acceptable, as long as it's on a phone.&#160;</p><p>The phone makes social media too instantly available. It promises that you'll never be bored again anywhere — at the in-laws, at the supermarket, in an elevator. And that's just awful.&#160;</p><p>We need to be bored, <a href=\"https://time.com/5480002/benefits-of-boredom/\">at least in moderation</a>. Mental health, creativity, and the ability to be entertained require brains to endure at least a little bit of empty space.</p><p>There was a moment a few years back, where after many years of \"social smoking\" at alcohol-soaked events, I decided once and for all that cigarettes were gross and not even worth the occasional \"social\" puff. This feels like that.&#160;</p><p>Last week, I tweeted a strong opinion. Can't remember what it was. But I did feel a familiar jones for the affirmation earned from sending very good non-ratioed takes. I had to walk away from my laptop after about a minute, and then I completely forgot about the tweet.&#160;</p><p>Reopening my computer a few hours later, there were a favorable amount of RTs and Faves, with a mere sprinkling of \"Go fuck yourself\" replies.&#160;</p><p>It was all there, the life story of that tweet. For about 20 minutes, a few hundred people cared enough to engage with it, and they mostly liked it. Then they forgot it, just like I already had.</p><p>The thrill is gone.</p><p>I don't reflexively reach for my phone anymore. After going from extremely online to just occasionally online, it's a lot easier to walk right past the <a href=\"http://sitn.hms.harvard.edu/flash/2018/dopamine-smartphones-battle-time/\">dopamine dealer</a>.&#160;</p><p>To misquote Nancy Reagan, \"Just Say No to Social Media on Your Phone.\"</p><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li>Read more:</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/make-to-go-delivery-cocktail-alcohol-sales-permanent-coronavirus-pandemic-2020-5\" data-analytics-position=\"83\" data-analytics-module=\"\">Make 'to-go' cocktail sales permanent</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trumps-devotion-cronyism-getting-people-killed-coronavirus-pandemic-covid-2020-5\" data-analytics-position=\"87\" 22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"Why buying real estate may be a bad deal for you amid the pandemic","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/real-estate-is-a-bad-deal-amid-the-pandemic-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f527c1ce6ff30001d4e7308?format=jpeg\" alt=\"House for sale\" height=\"3420\" width=\"4567\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tom Merton/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Buying a house amid the coronavirus pandemic might seem like a good idea, especially with mortgage rates historically low, but evidence that is piling up is making it look like a bad deal.</li>\n<li>A <a href=\"https://lendedu.com/blog/mortgages-during-coronavirus-report/\">LendEDU survey</a> in late August found that 55% of those who became homeowners amid the pandemic already regret the decision, mostly due to financial reasons.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.redfin.com/blog/low-mortgage-rates-increase-purchasing-power/\">Redfin found</a> that as of the end of July, lower mortgage rates had given buyers an extra 6.9% in purchase power, but house prices were up 8.2% year-over-year.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Surprisingly <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/us-mortgage-rate-falls-record-low-time-this-year-again-2020-8-1029479257\">low mortgage rates</a>, the ability to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/remote-work-here-to-stay-if-coronavirus-triggers-a-recession-2020-3\">work from anywhere</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-pandemic-shifted-prioritize-amenities-buying-a-home-2020-8\">the desire for one's own backyard</a> are unique aspects of the coronavirus pandemic that have inspired many to buy a house. Mortgage applications are <a href=\"https://www.mba.org/2020-press-releases/august/mortgage-applications-decrease-in-latest-mba-weekly-survey\">up 22%</a> compared to last year, showing that demand is immense.</p><p>But if you're keen on submitting your own application, you might want to reconsider.</p><p>The US is facing a housing shortage that only ratchets home prices up, according to a new <a href=\"https://www.redfin.com/blog/coronavirus-real-estate-housing-shortage/?utm_source=feedburner&utm_medium=feed&utm_campaign=Feed%3A+redfin_corporate+%28Redfin+Corporate+Blog%3A+Notes+on+Redfin%2C+technology%2C+real+estate+and+life+at+a+startup.%29rtup.%29\">Redfin analysis</a>. Meanwhile, a new <a href=\"https://lendedu.com/blog/mortgages-during-coronavirus-report/\">LendEDU</a> survey found that those who decided to become pandemic homeowners are already expressing buyer's remorse.</p><p>The number of homes for sale in the country was down for the 12th straight month in July. Just 1.9 million homes were on the market in July, according to <a href=\"https://www.redfin.com/blog/coronavirus-real-estate-housing-shortage/?utm_source=feedburner&utm_medium=feed&utm_campaign=Feed%3A+redfin_corporate+%28Redfin+Corporate+Blog%3A+Notes+on+Redfin%2C+technology%2C+real+estate+and+life+at+a+startup.%29rtup.%29\">Redfin.</a></p><p>The housing deficit, which already existed due to what Redfin called a \"homebuilding slowdown\" following the Great Recession, has only been exacerbated by the pandemic. Many are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/three-us-cities-people-are-looking-to-move-out-of-2020-8\">fleeing coastal capitals</a> and looking to relocate to more affordable metro areas while taking advantage of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/personal-finance/best-mortgage-refinance-rates-today-friday-september-4-2020\">all-time low mortgage rates.</a></p><p>Take Baltimore and San Antonio, for example. Both are notably more affordable housing markets — but their housing supply has plummeted 20% year-over-year amid the pandemic. Meanwhile, the supply in expensive cities like New York and San Francisco has surged, while demand dwindles.</p><p>In Baltimore, buyers outnumbering sellers has contributed to elevated home prices. \"Buyers are willing to pay more for a house than I've ever seen — I'm talking $30,000 to $50,000 over the listing price,\" Dan Borowy, a Baltimore real estate agent, told Redfin. \"They're desperate because homes are flying off the market so quickly. I'm selling all of the homes I'm listing within three days.\"</p><p>A new study shows those new homeowners almost immediately experienced buyer's remorse.</p><p><a href=\"https://lendedu.com/blog/mortgages-during-coronavirus-report/\">LendEDU</a> surveyed 1,000 homeowners with a mortgage in late August. More than half of respondents — a whopping 55% — reported that they regret taking out a mortgage amid the pandemic.</p><p>Roughly 30% of those with regrets cited financial struggles. Even with low interest rates, payments become more difficult to manage as the pandemic continues to sink the country into a recession.</p><p>Another 10% said social reasons fueled their regret, while 7% reported that they were not prepared for homeownership, and 8% reported another miscellaneous reason.</p><p>This may be down to the dynamics of the market. <a href=\"https://www.redfin.com/blog/low-mortgage-rates-increase-purchasing-power/\">Redfin calculated</a> that as of the end of July, the lower mortgage rates have given buyers an extra 6.9% in purchasing power, but prices were up 8.2% year-over-year, wiping that out.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Borden)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f527c1ce6ff30001d4e7308?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn4@2020_1/2020/09/06/14-05-16-272_7d0c67cd9124240d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn76@2020_4/2020/09/06/14-05-49-381_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=j5XYW7gkzDQ:lWuklCB9Plw:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn92@2020_4/2020/09/06/14-05-45-891_556e782a0733b6d9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=j5XYW7gkzDQ:lWuklCB9Plw:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn91@2020_6/2020/09/06/14-05-48-737_e9da102998186927.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn71@2020_5/2020/09/06/14-05-44-327_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=j5XYW7gkzDQ:lWuklCB9Plw:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn51@2020_1/2020/09/06/14-05-48-540_3ca24fb844a800a0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/j5XYW7gkzDQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn39@2020_3/2020/09/06/14-05-31-331_eb6773e0d22db97d.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599401096939},{"createdTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"A timeline of unfulfilled promises Trump made about his border wall, a cornerstone of his 2016 campaign which has faded from view in 2020","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/timeline-of-president-trumps-unfulfilled-border-wall-promises-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f522df17ed0ee001e25d76e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"trump border wall\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump tours a section of new U.S.-Mexico border wall in San Luis, Arizona, on June 23, 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Carlos Barria/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Since long before his presidency, Donald Trump has made the construction of a wall along the border with Mexico his keystone issue.&#160;</li>\n<li>Since it was first suggested &#8212; to rapturous applause &#8212; in 2014, the issue has arguably propelled Trump into the presidency.</li>\n<li>The Washington Post reported that Trump mentioned a wall more than 200 times in his 2016 campaign, though it has played only a bit part in 2020.</li>\n<li>Trump has made a dizzying array of claims about it. However, there is still no manmade physical barrier along much of the US-Mexico border.</li>\n<li>Here are some of the key claims he has made about the wall that have not come to pass.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>&#160;</p><p>Donald Trump's vision of a \"big, beautiful wall\" between the US and Mexico arguably did more than anything else in his 2016 platform to propel him into the White House.</p><p>Border security experts, and many of Trump's allies, have pointed out that a wall alone is too blunt an instrument to help much with US border security issues.&#160;</p><p>But the architect of the policy, Sam Nunberg <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/the-adviser-thought-up-trumps-wall-thinks-should-still-happen-2020-7\">earlier explained to Business Insider</a> that this lack of subtlety is exactly the point.&#160;</p><p>\"The wall in 2016 was symbolic of Donald Trump: common sense, practical solutions, simplified answers — as opposed to long nuanced, detailed policy speak,\" he said</p><p>Trump recently told a rally that the wall is \"almost complete\" — while his campaign website says 216 miles have been completed. It does not mention that the US-Mexico border is almost 2,000 miles long.</p><p>Here is a run-down of the major promises the president has made about the wall.</p><h2><strong>April 2014: \"I would build a border like nobody's seen before.\"</strong></h2><p>In April 2014, as Trump prepared to begin his bid for the Republican nomination, he made his first mention of a wall — or at least a fence — at a New Hampshire conservative event.&#160;</p><p>In preparing for <a href=\"https://www.c-span.org/video/?318743-2/donald-trump-freedom-summit\">his speech to the Freedom Summit</a>, advisers Sam Nunberg and Roger Stone struggled to remind Trump to center immigration in his speech. Trump was resolving to be \"the hardest on the Right\" on these issues, Nunberg later told Business Insider, but struggled to stick closely to prepared notes.</p><p>The simple idea of a wall appealed to Trump.&#160;</p><p>\"We either have to have borders, and I mean strong borders ... and I mean strong. And you know I'm a builder, I build great buildings,\" Trump told his audience.<br><br>\"Building a border, you know they talk about 'oh I don't know, how could we possibly build a fence that nobody can climb over?' I would build a border like nobody's seen before. Nobody's climbing over.\"</p><h2><strong>June 2015: </strong><strong>\"I will make Mexico pay for that wall.\"</strong></h2><p>As Trump announced his candidacy for the Republican nomination, a new promise arose — and it appears to have been totally off the cuff.<br><br>\"I will build a great, great wall on our southern border, and&#160;I will make Mexico pay for that wall,\" he said. \"Mark my words.\"<br><br>According to Ian Volner, who has chronicled the Trump wall in his book \"The Great Great Wall: Along the Borders of History from China to Mexico,\" the claim wasn't in the briefing notes circulated to journalists prior to his announcement speech.&#160;</p><p>His campaign quickly wound it back, qualifying the promise as it made headlines.&#160;</p><p>Whether Mexico was paying literally or figuratively didn't turn out to matter that much. <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/01/09/fact-checking-president-trumps-oval-office-address-immigration/\">According to The Washington Post</a>, Trump would go on to talk about a border wall more than 200 times on the tumultuous 2016 campaign trail.</p><h2><strong>August 24, 2015: It will have a \"very big, beautiful door\"</strong></h2><p>\"This will be a wall with a very big, very beautiful door, because we want the legals to come back into the country,\" Trump told CBS News.&#160;<br><br>A big door to welcome documented immigrants hasn't been given much attention since. <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TgPUk760vWw\">In a 2019 roundtable discussion on border security</a>, Trump remarked on the doorways in an existing section of wall and suggested not having any.</p><p>\"Because putting the doors on cost more than the property is worth,\" he said.&#160;</p><h2><strong>January 25 2017: He orders \"a contiguous, physical wall\" (or similar barrier).<br></strong></h2><p>Anti-immigration executive orders came at speed after Trump took office.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/presidential-actions/executive-order-border-security-immigration-enforcement-improvements/\">Border Security and Immigration Enforcement Improvements</a> set in officialese exactly what Trump meant by the wall — a definition that left room for the <a href=\"https://eu.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/onpolitics/2019/01/08/trump-wall-concept-timeline/2503855002/\">many, many visions</a> the president has described since.</p><p>\"'Wall' shall mean a contiguous, physical wall or other similarly secure, contiguous, and impassable physical barrier,\" read the order. With numerous natural barriers along the way, the amount of new construction has been reckoned at around 900 miles.</p><h2><strong>June 6, 2017: \"There is a chance that we can do a solar wall.\"</strong></h2><p>With this environmentally-friendly vision, proposed at a White House meeting with Republican congressional leaders, Trump suggested the costs of the wall could be covered by solar-power-generated electricity.</p><p>\"We are seriously looking at a solar wall,\" said Trump, pointing out that the sun-drenched border would offer obvious opportunity.&#160;</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-solar-border-wall-2017-7\">As Business Insider's Leanna Garfield reported at the time</a>, a solar-powered array could conceivably recuperate construction costs, but only over decades.&#160;</p><p>It was never mentioned again.</p><h2><strong>July 7 2017: Mexico will \"absolutely\" pay. This time, said with the Mexican president sitting next to him.&#160;</strong></h2><p><strong><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52545e7ed0ee001e25d842?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Trump Ernesto Nieto g20 summit hamburg 2017 wall mexico\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>U.S. President Donald Trump meets Mexico&#39;s President Enrique Pena Nieto during the G20 summit in Hamburg, Germany July 7, 2017\n<p class=\"copyright\">Carlos Barria/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></strong></p><p>It's not possible to list all the times Trump has repeated his claim that Mexico will foot the bill for the wall, but <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/01/11/us/politics/trump-mexico-pay-wall.html\">The New York Times made a fact-check</a> of the different ways that this could be done. These suggestions have ranged from cutting foreign aid to waiting for a literal check.&#160;</p><p>Trump said it again during a <a href=\"https://nymag.com/intelligencer/2017/07/trump-says-he-absolutely-wants-mexico-to-pay-for-wall.html\">G20 press conference in Hamburg</a> with Mexican president Enrique Peña Nieto did nothing to bring that closer to reality.&#160;</p><p>As of time of publication, an official Trump campaign page called \"Promises Kept\" makes no mention of ways in which Mexico has, or will, contribute.</p><h2><strong>April 2017: The wall will cost $21.6 billion</strong></h2><p>In 2017, the Department for Homeland Security priced the wall at $21.6 billion, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-trump-immigration-wall-exclusive/exclusive-trump-border-wall-to-cost-21-6-billion-take-3-5-years-to-build-internal-report-idUSKBN15O2ZN\">Reuters reported</a>.&#160;</p><p>Others disagreed. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-border-wall-billions-unseen-costs-gao-report-2018-8\">The Democratic Party asserted</a> it would be at least $70 billion — plus maintenance costs — while a non-partisan oversight committee simply said the DHS costing was far too low.&#160;&#160;</p><h2><strong>January 2018: He'll build it for even less than that, in a year</strong></h2><p>After another estimate suggested the wall would cost $18 billion, Trump ramped up expectations still further.&#160;</p><p>During an immigration policy negotiation with Democrats, he said: \"I can build it for less than that&#160; ... We can build the wall in one year and we can build it for much less money than what they're talking about,\" <a href=\"https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-5252639/Trump-build-wall-budget-ahead-schedule.html\">according to MailOnline</a>.</p><p>He went on to talk about the Wollman Rink, an ice rink languishing under failed municipal repair and a spiraling budget until 1986, when he offered to take over the refurbishment. He completed it in four months and 25% under budget.&#160;</p><p>However, with the scrutiny of Congress, he has not been able to repeat this success with his border wall.&#160;</p><h2>December 21, 2019: Government shutdown</h2><p>In mid-December, as Congress was wrangling with the president over the next year's funding bill, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/government-shutdown-trump-border-wall-demands-deadlocks-congress-2018-12\">Trump made a late-notice demand for $5 billion for his wall</a> — much more than the $1.6 billion that the Democrats countered with for general border-security funding.</p><p>The standoff triggered a government shutdown that lastest well into the new year.&#160;</p><p>Trump begrudgingly agreed to a package including $1.4 billion for barrier construction on January 15, ending the shutdown.&#160;</p><h2><strong>January 10, 2019: No wall, renewed talk of Mexico paying</strong></h2><p>A year after his self-imposed deadline, there was no completed wall. Instead, there were more attempts to salvage the idea that Mexico might foot the bill.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-mexico-write-check-for-border-wall-2019-1\">On January 10, Trump said</a>: \"When, during the campaign, I would say Mexico is going to pay for it, obviously I never said this and I never meant they're going to write out a check.\"</p><p>Instead, he said, Mexico will pay \"indirectly,\" through renegotiated trade deals. As Business Insider's Bob Bryan explained, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-oval-office-shutdown-speech-usmca-trade-deal-pay-border-wall-2019-1\">that's not how it works</a>.&#160;</p><h2>February 15, 2019: Trump declares a national emergency</h2><p>After the debacle of the government shutdown, Trump's next move was to declare the situation at the border <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-declares-national-emergency-build-border-wall-2019-2\">a national emergency</a>, enabling him to bypass Congress and approve billions in funding for his wall.&#160;</p><p>As he announced it, he told reporters: \"I could do the wall over a longer period of time. I didn't need to do this. But I'd rather do it much faster.\"<br><br>Another $3.8 billion was raided from the Pentagon's budget for the wall, which was considered a \"higher priority item,\" <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2020/02/13/805796618/trump-administration-diverts-3-8-billion-in-pentagon-funding-to-border-wall\">NPR reported</a>.</p><h2><strong>June 2020: Trump says Biden will finish the wall if he gets elected<br></strong></h2><p>With the project clearly not going to plan, and an election looming, <a href=\"https://www.mediaite.com/news/trump-claims-joe-biden-will-finish-border-wall-because-therell-be-a-revolution-if-he-doesnt/\">Trump told Fox 10 in Phoenix</a> that the wall would continue even if he loses.</p><p>He predicted that Joe Biden would have to continue the project or there would be a \"revolution.\" <a href=\"https://www.foxnews.com/politics/biden-border-wall-construction-stop-elected\">Biden soon said the opposite</a>: if he is elected, construction will stop.</p><h2><strong>August 18, 2020: \"Almost complete\" — even though it is far from it.<br></strong></h2><p>Trump, and his campaign, have made many different claims about how done the wall is. On the campaign trail on August 28, <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Md8tIz-oblQ\">Trump told New Hampshire</a> that the wall is \"almost complete.\"</p><p>Yet on the Trump campaign website \"Promises Kept,\" the wall's completion <a href=\"https://www.promiseskept.com/achievement/overview/immigration/\">is discussed in the present tense</a>.&#160;</p><p>\"Pres. Trump is fulfilling his promise to build a border wall, with large portions finished or under construction,\" says the site.&#160;</p><p>The Trump campaign states that 216 miles have been completed, \"with an additional 339 miles under construction and 183 miles under pre-construction.\" It is not clear what \"pre-construction\" is.</p><p>But what we do know is that most of that was a replacement wall. As of May 2020, only three miles has been built on fresh ground, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2020/05/26/theres-new-wall-194-miles-border-16-miles-didnt-have-wall-before/\">The Washington Post reported</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"Airbus just unveiled its new $14 million luxury helicopter that can seat up to 10 people — see inside","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbus-luxury-helicopter-seat-10-people-for-around-14-million-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d37b2cdf25a001e84e213?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbus ACH160\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Airbus&#39; ACH160 helicopter.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.airbus.com/helicopters/civil-helicopters/medium/h160.html\" target=\"_blank\">Airbus</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\"><li>Airbus is turning its <a href=\"https://www.airbus.com/helicopters/civil-helicopters/medium/h160.html\">H160</a> aircraft into a luxury helicopter for business or private use: the ACH160.</li><li>Airbus Corporate Helicopters (ACH) is the company's high-end bespoke segment that's catered to private clients and business use.</li><li>The ACH160 starts at over $14 million, although this price shifts depending on different add-ons and equipment in the customizable interior.</li><li>The luxury helicopter will be available for delivery later this year.</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li></ul><p>Airbus is creating a luxury version of its <a href=\"https://www.airbus.com/helicopters/civil-helicopters/medium/h160.html\">H160</a> helicopter: the ACH160, which starts at around $14 million for business or private use.</p><p>The <a href=\"http://www.airbuscorporatehelicopters.com/website/en/ref/ACH160_266.html\">ACH160</a> is the \"premium\" iteration of the H160 and the latest aircraft in the ACH line, which includes six other corporate helicopters that can be tailored per customer. Despite these differences in luxury levels, both the ACH160 and H160 will be available deliveries later this year, <a href=\"https://www.airbus.com/newsroom/press-releases/en/2020/07/italian-order-highlights-continuing-success-of-ach160.html\">according to Airbus</a>.</p><p>The customizable aspects inside the luxury helicopter include seating, with options like bench-style seats, individual seats, or a mix of both, for a total accommodation of up to 10 passengers. This tailored configuration has also already been employed in the latest ACH160 order for a client in Italy, who requested the helicopter with a bespoke six-seater configuration, <a href=\"http://www.airbuscorporatehelicopters.com/website/en/press/Italian-order-highlights-continuing-success-of-ACH160_34.html\">according to Airbus</a>.</p><p>Keep scrolling to see inside the ACH160 which starts at around $14 million, although this price can vary based on aspects like equipment, configurations, and finishes, an Airbus spokesperson told Business Insider:</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tBesides the Italy-based customer, the luxury helicopter has also been ordered in eight other countries in Europe, China, Southeast Asia, and Latin and North helicopter.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.airbus.com/helicopters/civil-helicopters/medium/h160.html\" target=\"_blank\">Airbus</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAccording to its maker, the ACH160's design is backed by 68 new patents.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d390ccdf25a001e84e223?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbus ACH160\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2222\" target=\"_blank\">Airbus</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tLike any luxury aircraft, the inside of the ACH160 is lined with leather, wood veneers, and a handmade carpet.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d3a8ecdf25a001e84e231?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbus ACH160\" height=\"1250\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Airbus&#39; ACH160 helicopter.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"https://www.airbus.com/helicopters/civil-helicopters/medium/h160.html\" target=\"_blank\">Airbus</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe ACH160 has a maximum cruising speed of 155 knots, or about 178.4 miles-per-hour, and a range of 852 kilometers, about 529.4 miles.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d3bf242f43f001ddfdc02?format=jpeg\" ...\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d3a3642f43f001ddfdbf2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbus ACH160\" height=\"1667\" width=\"2222\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Airbus&#39; ACH160 payload of over 1.1 tons for trips within 138.1 miles.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d3be7cdf25a001e84e239?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbus ACH160\" height=\"1406\" width=\"1875\" the older generation of engines.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d3b98cdf25a001e84e235?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbus ACH160\" height=\"1533\" width=\"2044\" flight deck from Helionix, decreasing the amount of work that the pilot has to handle, according to Airbus.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d3a6742f43f001ddfdbf5?format=jpeg\" blades.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3d3a6242f43f001ddfdbf4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Airbus ACH160\" height=\"1728\" width=\"2304\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Airbus&#39; ACH160 Trump has shown he protects America and us by extension from foreign threats by obliterating terrorists at the root and before they get a chance to strike,\" she told the tabloid.&#160;</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Noor Bin Ladin  (@NoorBinLadin) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1262120584688926720?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">May 17, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>&#160;</p><p>She told the publication that she lives in Switzerland, and her branch of the family has always spelled their name differently to her uncle, the notorious leader of the al Qaeda terrorist organization, and the 9/11 mastermind.&#160;</p><p>in Ladin told the publication that she was a longtime admirer of Trump, whose pledge to ban Muslims from the US was one of the main planks of his 2016 election bid (a modified version of the ban was declared legal by the US Supreme Court in 2018.)</p><p>The president had pledged to pursue tougher anti-terror policies than the Obama administration, but has been <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/isis-could-regroup-amid-trump-fueled-chaos-in-syria-2019-10\">accused of pursuing a chaotic foreign policy </a>that has allowed the ISIS fighters to regroup in Syria&#160;</p><p>\"I have been a supporter of President Trump since he announced he was running in the early days in 2015. father, whose family fortune was in construction in Saudi Arabia.</p><p>She told the Post that she has degrees in business administration from the University of Geneva and commercial law from the University of London, and was penning a book on international relations.&#160;</p><p>Noor's sister, Wafah Dufour, is a socialite and indie rock singer, whose band, Deep Tan, toured Europe last year, bin Ladin said that growing up in the West meant she had a strong appreciation of western liberal values.&#160;</p><p>\"My life would have been very different had I been raised in Saudi Arabia,\" she upgrades that can further implement more luxury amenities into the tiny home on wheels, such as a spa bathroom, guest bed stored in the ceiling of the trailer, and a home office.</p><p>The new 2021 Living Vehicle trailer comes in <a href=\"https://www.livingvehicle.com/models\">three versions</a>: the $229,995 Core, $289,995 Max, and $369,995 Pro. However, the only difference between the three are the power systems and weights.</p><p>The Core, Max, and Pro are all powered by Volta Power Systems' lithium-ion battery, which can also double as an electric vehicle charger if the trailer is being towed by an EV.</p><p>Keep scrolling to see inside the new ultra-luxe 2021 model:</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tThe 2021 Living Vehicle trailer's exterior is made of aluminum with stainless steel components, but no wood.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f4fb2ab7ed0ee001e25cfbd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The 2021 Living Vehicle travel trailer\" height=\"1250\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The 2021 Living Vehicle travel trailer while on the road.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a temperature-sensitive power and water supplies, and technology.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f4fb29ce6ff30001d4e69b3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The 2021 Living Vehicle travel trailer\"
