22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"French company Flying Whales is creating an airship that can pickup and drop cargo without landing — see how","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/flying-whales-lca60t-airship-can-move-cargo-without-landing-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f50f41c7ed0ee001e25d386?format=jpeg\" alt=\"LCA60T_wood\" height=\"1559\" width=\"2079\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying Whales&#39; LCA60T aircraft in the woods.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://flying-whales.com/en\" target=\"_blank\">Flying Whales</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>France-based Flying Whales is developing an environmentally friendly cargo transport aircraft with commercial production posied to begin in 2025.</li>\n<li>The LCA60T airship can off-load its up to 66-ton payload mid-air.</li>\n<li>Because the LCA60T is a VTOL, it won't require any extra infrastructure to operate, allowing it to serve more remote locations without harming the environment.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"http://flying-whales.com/en\">Flying Whales</a> is producing a blimp-like aircraft that can transport and drop off cargo mid-flight.</p><p>Several components of the cargo transport airship are made to be environmentally friendly, such as its floating capabilities powered by helium, hybrid-electric propulsion system, and lack of need for extra infrastructure during take-offs and landings.</p><p>But don't get confused by its oblong shape and helium-powered floating capabilities: the LCA60T&#160; is rigid and can't be \"deflated\", setting it apart from the traditional blimp despite its exterior appearance.</p><p>The aircraft was originally designed to transport wood logs around inaccessible areas by creating an airship that didn't need infrastructure support. However, the France-based team quickly pivoted to a larger, less targeted client base, the team told Business Insider.</p><p>\"We realized that this solution could be used in a lot of other sectors, so the [later] goal was not to make something that was only able to work for wood transport,\" Romain Schalck, marketing manager for Flying Whales, told Business Insider. \"But we wanted to start with something because it's, generally speaking, easier to start designing something to answer a specific market.\"</p><p>In terms of other iterations, Flying Whales is currently working with both state and private financial supporters and clients across various industries in Europe, Asia, and Canada, with plans to eventually expand to the US as the team grows in the future.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tAs of right now, one of the company's biggest investors is the Aviation Industry Corporation of China (AVIC). The same year AVIC first called Flying Whales (2017), the company also received an investment from the French state of around $29.5 million, according to Schalck.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f50f6e07ed0ee001e25d390?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Flying Whales LCA60T aircraft _wood2\" height=\"1405\" width=\"1874\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying Whales&#39; LCA60T aircraft in the woods.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://flying-whales.com/en\" target=\"_blank\">Flying Whale</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Around then, the company started expanding from its team of five to six people, to 50 employees.</p><p>Now, Flying Whales has over 130 employees with plans to expand even more when the group starts shifting from an engineering to an industrial company, which will come when it's ready to start physically producing the airships.</p><p>\"Maybe at the end of the program development, we will be close to 300 people in the design office,\" Pierre-Yves Fouillen, market manager at Flying Whale, told Business Insider. \"Once we start to operate the airships, the number of employees will just explode.\"</p>\n\tFlying Whales plans to build its first factory in France in the coming year with the goal of having the first LCA60T in the air by 2024.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f50f6e8e6ff30001d4e6d49?format=jpeg\" alt=\"LCA60T_wood\" height=\"1482\" width=\"1976\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying Whales&#39; LCA60T aircraft in the woods.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://flying-whales.com/en\" target=\"_blank\">Flying Whale</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Commercial production is poised to begin in 2025, and the final goal is to make over 162 LCA60Ts in the first decade of production.</p>\n\tAs of now, the price of the aircraft is confidential, but according to the Flying Whales team, its tag is closer to that of a helicopter than a plane.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f50f6f17ed0ee001e25d391?format=jpeg\" alt=\"LCA60T_wind blades\" height=\"1428\" width=\"1904\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying Whales&#39; LCA60T aircraft carrying several wind blades.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://flying-whales.com/en\" target=\"_blank\">Flying Whale</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>The company also plans to develop an \"ownership operator\" segment of its business that will allow clients to use the airships for short-term projects instead of having to purchase an entire unit just for one mission.</p>\n\tThe rigidity of the structure that sets the LCA60T apart from a blimp is its \"multilayer envelope technology,\" which uses several thin layers of textile fabric panels — similar to that of an inflatable boat — over the actual structure, according to Schalck.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f50f6f87ed0ee001e25d392?format=jpeg\" alt=\"LCA60T_pipeline\" height=\"1874\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying Whales&#39; LCA60T carrying part of a pipeline.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://flying-whales.com/en\" target=\"_blank\">Flying Whale</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>And since the air vehicle uses helium to hover, the LCA60T has a low fuel consumption compared to traditional aircrafts.</p>\n\tThe airship can also load and remove cargo while hovering, which is done by employing winches that are controlled by a \"loadmaster.\"\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f50f6fe7ed0ee001e25d393?format=jpeg\" alt=\"LCA60T_electrical tower\" height=\"1414\" width=\"1892\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying Whales&#39; LCA60T aircraft carrying an electrical tower.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://flying-whales.com/en\" target=\"_blank\">Flying Whale</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>Despite its 66-ton payload, the LCA60T can carry objects of any size or shape by using slings that hang under the aircraft, although there's also a cargo holding area inside.</p><p>The LCA60T can cruise at around 62 miles-per-hour with the aim of doing \"short\" &#8212; within around 124 to 186 miles &#8212; trips.</p>\n\tThe LCA60T has vertical take-off and landing capabilities, which means additional infrastructures like runways won't be needed just to operate the aircraft.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f50f70e7ed0ee001e25d394?format=jpeg\" alt=\"LCA60T_desert\" height=\"845\" width=\"1690\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying Whales&#39; LCA60T aircraft in the desert.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://flying-whales.com/en\" target=\"_blank\">Flying Whale</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<p>According to Schalck, the lack of any extra infrastructure means remote areas can be accessed without harming the environment.</p><p>The hybrid electric propulsion system that powers the airship also gives Flying Whales the opportunity to then shift to full electric propulsion in the future, further decreasing the airship's carbon footprint.</p><p>\"We decided to equip the first airship with a hybrid propulsion first because we think today, we are in a world in which we cannot create new industrial tools without taking into account the protection of the environment,\" Schalck said. \"A hybrid electric propulsion is not the perfect saver for the environment, but it's a good first step.\"</p>\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a (Brittany Chang)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f50f41c7ed0ee001e25d386?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn68@2020_1/2020/09/06/14-05-52-170_e370dde1e3771ed9.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f50f6e07ed0ee001e25d390?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn23@2020_4/2020/09/06/14-05-49-906_6249c8fe02b48efe.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f50f6e8e6ff30001d4e6d49?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn76@2020_5/2020/09/06/14-05-38-339_0f0054bfc07af30b.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f50f6f17ed0ee001e25d391?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn24@2020_1/2020/09/06/14-05-46-151_f23ab8fae55d6bd6.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f50f6f87ed0ee001e25d392?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn99@2020_2/2020/09/06/14-05-36-115_3cc0a3beb8cf8c87.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f50f6fe7ed0ee001e25d393?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn91@2020_2/2020/09/06/14-05-29-778_e02ca98d87591aeb.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f50f70e7ed0ee001e25d394?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn24@2020_1/2020/09/06/14-05-48-981_ca44d4a69def9784.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn76@2020_4/2020/09/06/14-05-49-381_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=274DteXsqnA:MDlWr_e52PA:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn79@2020_3/2020/09/06/14-05-47-019_ed43a3fdabf25e7e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=274DteXsqnA:MDlWr_e52PA:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn32@2020_6/2020/09/06/14-05-51-713_1b2334556b22be0c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn71@2020_5/2020/09/06/14-05-44-327_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=274DteXsqnA:MDlWr_e52PA:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn8@2020_4/2020/09/06/14-05-46-301_c400f9760f4c17d5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/274DteXsqnA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn63@2020_2/2020/09/06/14-05-41-519_86ffdd9a7dd01f74.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599401096943},{"createdTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"Tesla's cars are too expensive, and Elon Musk knows it — here's why that could be a big problem for the electric-vehicle leader","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/teslas-are-too-expensive-why-that-could-be-a-problem-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5eb959773dac9a7119588d35?format=jpeg\" alt=\"elon musk\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1778\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla CEO Elon Musk knows his cars cost too much.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><br >\n<ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Over the course of about two decades, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-monopoly-electric-car-market-2018-12\">Tesla has established a micro-monopoly</a> over the electric car market.</li>\n<li>But to survive, it has had to charge a lot for its vehicles, which runs counter to CEO Elon Musk's master plan to kill off the internal-combustion engine.</li>\n<li>It's possible that Tesla will never face meaningful EV competition, despite numerous companies jumping into the action.</li>\n<li>But eventually, Tesla could end up monopolizing data, and that would lead to problems for the company.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Silicon Valley's biggest problem is that it hates competition. And by hates, I mean structurally despises it, from soup to nuts: venture capitalists pretty much want to invest only in startups that promise to completely dominate markets, raking in as close to 100% of potential gains as possible.</p><p>It wasn't always like this: The first wave of technology firms, from Hewlett-Packard to Apple to Microsoft, emerged from the model of fierce, government-monitored competition, leading to a lot of innovation and a beneficial mix of great products and great prices. That's how we got computers on our desks, on our laps, and in our pockets when, decades ago, they required entire buildings.</p><p>The second wave of tech innovation, based on the internet and later mobile computing, turned venture capitalists into venture monopolists. That why we now have so few companies providing vast numbers of uses with essential digital products and services. And this state of affairs has been valorized, notably by PayPal co-founder Peter Thiel, who infamously (and influentially) argued in 2014 that the conventional wisdom concerning monopolies is bogus.</p><p>\"All happy companies are different: Each one earns a monopoly by solving a unique problem,\" <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/peter-thiel-competition-is-for-losers-1410535536#:~:text=Monopolies%20are%20a%20good%20thing%20for%20society%2C%20venture%20capitalist%20Peter,in%20an%20essay%20on%20WSJ.&text=The%20opposite%20of%20perfect%20competition,can%20set%20its%20own%20prices.ces.\">he wrote in a Wall Street Journal op-ed</a> to support his book, <em>Zero to One: Notes on Startups, or How to Build the Future. \"</em>All failed companies are the same: They failed to escape competition,\" he added, riffing on Tolstoy's insight.</p><h2>An unhappy Elon Musk</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e6a8435e4f9fe21de44f5f4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"peter thiel\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1777\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Peter Thiel is a fan of monopolies.\n<p class=\"copyright\">J. Scott Applewhite/AP</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>It isn't worth debating whether Thiel is right or wrong. A successful business wants to aspire to the condition of monopoly, full stop. But that raises the question, \"Is that good for customers?\" And while the answer can be yes, a dynamic, capitalist economy has usually encouraged robust competition on the assumption that the key to consumer happiness is a fair market price, not a price established by one player and then charged as what economist term a \"rent.\"</p><p>Thiel's PayPal partner, Elon Musk, has found himself in a situation that, with just a bit of a stretch, fits the definition of a monopoly. Tesla is selling nearly all the electric cars that consumers are buying. Various competing products from startups and incumbents aren't making a dent in Tesla's business. And Tesla is taking advantage.</p><p>In general, the auto industry is a good example of how competition has led to a lot of consumer choice and a degree of predictability about prices. A Toyota Corolla is going to be a good car, and it's going to cost about $20,000, base. Likewise, a Honda Civic. There's abundant demand for cars at that price, and so the market in the US has performed superbly in inviting companies to meet that demand.</p><p>In the electric-vehicle space, however, demand isn't being met. It's almost impossible to buy an affordable, new EV, one that costs less than $500 per month on a typical auto loan. Tesla's cheapest Model 3 sedan is $38,000.</p><p>Musk is aware of this, and he isn't happy about it. His overarching goal is to get as many EVs on the roads as possible, Tesla-badged or otherwise. But for now, Tesla needs to sell expensive EVs to survive. Ironically, survival has yielded a monopoly, and Wall Street recognizes it: That's why Tesla's shares are up over 8,000% from the company's 2010 IPO and the market cap now exceeds every other carmaker's, along with those of some of America's biggest companies.</p><h2>Musk doesn't care about money</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f11a75ef0f419238243bb92?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FILE PHOTO: Tesla Inc CEO Elon Musk dances onstage during a delivery event for Tesla China-made Model 3 cars in Shanghai, China January 7, 2020. REUTERS/Aly Song/File Photo\" height=\"1982\" width=\"2643\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla is operating or building factories on three continents.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>If Musk had his way, he'd keep building factories and EVs all over the world, using Wall Street as an ATM to fund the expansion, and get millions of electric vehicles on the road in the next decade while losing money on everything. To be honest, that could be construed as a virtuous monopoly. Amazon, after all, has at times been content to remain profitless while offering consumers almost everything they want, from swift deliveries to rock-bottom prices.&#160;</p><p>However, Tesla is on the way to owning the entire EV market and capturing all of its future global growth, as a matter of course. Barriers to competitive entry are very, very high — it's monumentally expensive to develop and manufacture just one automobile — but the established carmakers who have the money and expertise haven't taken any meaningful market share away from Tesla, and it's unclear whether startups such as Rivian and Lucid have the potential to catch up.</p><p>In the jargon of investing, Tesla doesn't just have a protective moat — it has a veritable ocean.</p><p>In this respect, Tesla is the greatest monopoly Silicon Valley has yet produced. And nobody seems particularly troubled by it. Except for Musk, who'd like to sell a cheaper car, and folks like me, who value market competition for its own sake. Thiel would insist that competing to compete is bad business because you end up competing away your profits and eventually go out of business, but so what? No business should be forever, and a business's erosion of profits just means that consumers are getting what they want or need at a great price.</p><p>Well, there is one other concerned party: the federal government, which is supposed to regulate the business realm to avoid monopolies and steward capitalist competition. Tesla is too small, and in too broadly competitive a market (autos generally, not just EVs) to attract antitrust actions. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tesla-monopoly-electric-car-market-2018-12\">I've called Tesla's achievement a micro-monopoly</a>, which is different from the real thing, but Tesla is preparing to scale up significantly, with new factories coming online, under construction, or planned for three continents.</p><h2>It's the data that matters</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/56a775b4c08a80880e8bc5a2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Tesla autopilot\" height=\"1610\" width=\"2880\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Tesla&#39;s Autopilot is a data-gathering powerhouse.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tesla</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>So it's fair to assume that the micro-monopoly could be macro, in a decade or so. It wouldn't shock me if, in that scenario, Musk builds a $10,000 EV and sells it at a big loss, simply to execute his master plan. Imagine a world where one in four Americans, perhaps more, drives a Tesla. The traditional auto industry consolidates into two or three mega-manufacturers. Consumer choice is drastically reduced.</p><p>And now we have to consider that the largest business opportunity in transportation isn't selling cars. It's acquiring data, through networked vehicles. No one is sure who's going to end up owning this data, but for Silicon Valley, the paradigm is obvious: The network facilitator does. Facebook makes money off your updates, Google makes money off your searches.&#160;</p><p>This is the point at which Tesla could run into trouble with its monopoly power. The simple reason is that some critical aspects of its vehicle systems won't work without donated data. Autopilot, Tesla's semi-self-driving technology, already requires the entire fleet to donate data to shared learning.</p><p>Interestingly, a challenge to Tesla's monopoly, if this all comes to pass, would probably delight Musk. Because that would mean that Tesla got as big as he dreamed it would be, and the internal-combustion engine was killed off by competition malfunctioning for just long enough to save the planet from global warming. Maybe monopolies aren't so bad, after all. Just make them temporary.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/teslas-are-too-expensive-why-that-could-be-a-problem-2020-9'>Business src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3c11c27f9786001d1f89a3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"trump v biden donors 2x1\" height=\"1025\" width=\"2050\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tom Pennington/Getty Images; SAUL LOEB/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The election in November is the most consequential in modern history, as a Trump win could mean further descent into fascism.</li>\n<li>Biden is currently up in the polls, but in order to send the right message to Americans, and the world abroad, Biden must defeat Trump in a landslide.</li>\n<li>Michael Gordon has a long history in marketing and communications strategy and Democratic politics.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>As we begin the typical homestretch of an atypical presidential campaign, there are four words that need to be repeated by every Democrat, everyone who believes in science, everyone who believes that unity makes us more powerful: it can't be close.</p><p>Democrats have a historic opportunity to repudiate all things Trump in November. This election is more than the two white septuagenarian men atop each ticket. It's about honoring truth, restoring American values, and shining a light on justice.</p><p>In order to punctuate the clearest mandate possible, former Vice President Joe Biden and the Senate Democrats need to win big. It can't be close.</p><h2><strong>The Republicans need to bend the rules</strong></h2><p>With our country's<a href=\"https://www.axios.com/demographic-shifts-what-matters-2020-424161bf-1e6e-4da9-b2b2-9a6b2b2099fa.html\"> ever-changing demographics</a>, Republicans need to bend the rules of the game to win. And they've become quite good at it. Whether it's trumpeting basically nonexistent<a href=\"https://www.brennancenter.org/issues/ensure-every-american-can-vote/vote-suppression/myth-voter-fraud\"> voter fraud</a> or<a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2019/dec/18/wisconsin-rightwing-group-will-voter-purge\"> purging voter rolls</a> or<a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2020-election/gerrymandering-alive-well-coming-battle-will-be-bigger-ever-n1106951\"> gerrymandering the map</a> or fear-mongering about<a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2020/08/28/906676695/ignoring-fbi-and-fellow-republicans-trump-continues-assault-on-mail-in-voting\"> mail-in voting</a>, Republicans work particularly hard at making sure many people — and especially people of color —&#160; don't get to participate in democracy.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2018/11/how-voter-suppression-actually-works/575035/\">In Georgia in 2018</a>, a combination of closed polling sites, long lines, and canceled voter registrations by the Republican gubernatorial candidate created the narrowest GOP victory in half a century, 1.39%.&#160;</p><p>During primaries this spring and summer in<a href=\"https://www.vox.com/2020/5/20/21263596/republican-voter-suppresion-failed-wisconsin-supreme-court\"> Wisconsin</a>,<a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/06/09/us/politics/atlanta-voting-georgia-primary.html\"> Georgia</a>, and several other states, we saw the lengths to which Republicans will go to<a href=\"https://theglobepost.com/2020/08/07/voter-suppression-pandemic/\"> take advantage of the pandemic</a> to suppress turnout. We should expect more of the same this fall, as the Trump campaign and the GOP launch<a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/08/13/politics/trump-campaign-voter-fraud-lawsuit-pennsylvania/index.html\"> lawsuits</a> to suppress the vote,<a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trumps-suggestion-of-deploying-law-enforcement-officials-to-monitor-polls-raises-specter-of-intimidation/2020/08/21/4ff6407a-e3bb-11ea-8dd2-d07812bf00f7_story.html\"> encourage voter intimidation</a>, and<a href=\"https://thehill.com/blogs/blog-briefing-room/news/503937-celebrities-and-politicians-speak-out-over-90-cut-in-polling\"> close down polling sites</a>.</p><p>The drama at the intersection of election day and the US Postal Service takes Republican manipulation to new depths. It's hard to know how much of an advantage these latest distortions of democracy give Republicans out of the gate – but we saw what they did in Georgia, and they're adding mail manipulation to that.</p><p>That means that the true Democratic victories in battleground states need to be sizable enough to overcome the warped factor.</p><p>Trump also is working hard to<a href=\"https://www.huffpost.com/entry/donald-trump_n_5f3d93cfc5b609f4f6740d37?guccounter=1&guce_referrer=aHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuZ29vZ2xlLmNvbS8&guce_referrer_sig=AQAAAAVezLbcORIT2DKAKgBpkT5PFmFCpPnhIKehotlFIa1UsiRrMO8dHSf3FAdEH1i7LzL4SP72BP3yutAb3KNF8iF56zQU2q0kQuhfvvgEFzunsVV7r-Zk36u4qqztDsMP9CoyjpdcHndkHUDAulvXYjYQeWiaOei3xZgJiOwCb2L3iOwCb2L3\"> undermine the election results</a> but with a big enough loss, he'll be exposed as the sore loser he is.</p><p>It can't be close.</p><h2><strong>Every Vote Matters</strong></h2><p>Republicans act like they win in a landslide even when they lose the popular vote – or win by a single state – or win by one Supreme Court Justice. And if Democrats win narrowly, they should govern with just as much confidence – but the mandate and the message will be much clearer in a landslide than in a squeaker.</p><p>To every Democrat, every disaffected Republican, and every swing voter: make sure you and everyone you know has a plan to vote. If you're mailing in your ballot, send it on the first date possible. If you're going in person, bring a mask, a book, and a snack. There will be many MAGAs who will try to deny you your voting power. They are doing that because they can't win on the merits. They can only win with intimidation.</p><p>Every volunteer who is comfortable traveling should go to a swing state and help ensure that people who want to vote can cast their ballot safely and easily. Volunteers who aren't traveling can work the phones in battleground states to do their part. Donate to<a href=\"https://nationalvoterregistrationday.org/\"> organizations</a> that are<a href=\"https://www.whenweallvote.org/about-us/\"> registering voters</a>, particularly in communities of color.</p><p>There are many more people who think the country is<a href=\"https://www.marketwatch.com/story/eight-in-10-americans-say-the-country-is-heading-in-the-wrong-direction-new-poll-shows-2020-07-27\"> heading in the wrong direction</a> than who think we are great again. There are many more people who are<a href=\"https://www.usnews.com/news/politics/articles/2020-03-05/most-americans-dislike-the-way-donald-trump-conducts-himself-survey-finds\"> disgusted with this president</a> than who love him. There are many more people who support<a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2019/09/10/759193047/poll-most-americans-want-to-see-congress-pass-gun-restrictions\"> common sense gun safety</a>,<a href=\"https://news.gallup.com/poll/316106/two-three-americans-support-racial-justice-protests.aspx\"> racial justice</a>,<a href=\"https://www.vox.com/energy-and-environment/2020/6/23/21298065/climate-clean-energy-public-opinion-poll-trends-pew\"> climate action</a>, and<a href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2020/06/17/americans-broadly-support-legal-status-for-immigrants-brought-to-the-u-s-illegally-as-children/\"> DACA</a> than who want to block progress.</p><p>We just need to prove it all on election day: It. Can't. Be. Close.</p><p><em>Michael has a long history in marketing and communications strategy and Democratic politics. He worked in the Clinton administration and as spokesperson for the Clinton Justice Department. He also has served on multiple national, state, and local campaigns.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5117b87ed0ee001e25d475?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air\" height=\"1321\" width=\"1761\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The modern-day air taxi isn't a futuristic vertical take-off and land aircraft but often a propeller aircraft that's inexpensive to operate and can comfortably fly passengers on regional routes.&#160;</li>\n<li>Hopscotch Air provides air taxi flights from airports across the Northeast as a cost-effective alternative to chartering a traditional private aircraft and time-effective alternative to driving.</li>\n<li>I flew on one of Hopscotch Air's air taxis between two airports in Long Island to see if it truly beat driving.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The idea of an air taxi for most is the futuristic concept of self-flying eVTOLs soaring over traffic-ridden city streets, flying passengers to their meetings across town. While that may be a reality of urban air mobility one day, the modern-day air taxi is completely different.&#160;</p><p>Hopscotch Air is a New York-based air taxi service that uses light aircraft to connect remote cities across the Northeast as a cost-effective alternative to chartering a private aircraft. Ideal for regional travel, CEO Andrew Schmertz views the firm's competitors to be more trains and automobiles than it does private jets and offers the convenience and exclusivity of a private aircraft experience without the costly extras the drive up the price.</p><p>Powering the air taxi fleet is the Cirrus SR-20/22 series of piston aircraft, one of the most popular in general aviation known for their comfort, style, and high tech systems.</p><p>I took a ride on a quick demonstration flight across Long Island between Farmingdale's Republic Airport and Brookhaven Airport to see whether the service is worth the premium compared to driving or taking a commercial flight.</p><p>Here's what it was like.&#160;</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tThis is an air taxi, operated by Hopscotch Air.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51133e7ed0ee001e25d45d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tFour of these piston engine-powered Cirrus SR-20/22 series aircraft currently make up the Hopscotch Air fleet, offering regional travel across the Northeast and beyond.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51132ce6ff30001d4e6dde?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tFrom New York, the aircraft have a range of around five hours, making cities like Chicago, Savannah, and Nashville all accessible with a non-stop flight when the weather allows.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511314e6ff30001d4e6dd7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tCirrus' aircraft are widely-regarded to be the Cadillac of piston aircraft thanks to its speed, comfort, and advanced onboard systems.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51132de6ff30001d4e6ddf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Aircraft</a></em></p>\n\tThey even have baggage compartments that can fit golf clubs or full-size luggage.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51133b7ed0ee001e25d459?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIncluding the pilot, the typical SR-20/22 can seat four passengers.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511316e6ff30001d4e6dd8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tOnly one pilot is required to fly the plane, leaving what's normally the co-pilot's seat open for a passenger.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113347ed0ee001e25d447?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air throughout.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113327ed0ee001e25d444?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" on the street but can be found at airports across the New York area. Our cab stand for the flight was Farmingdale's Republic Airport on Long Island.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511329e6ff30001d4e6dda?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tHopscotch Air uses private terminals, known as fixed-base operators or FBOs, so passengers can skip the security checkpoint and long lines that they'd face when taking an airliner.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511331e6ff30001d4e6de4?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" vertically for easy access but passengers do have to climb up on the wing to get in.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113247ed0ee001e25d438?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI settled into the co-pilot's seat for the first leg of our trip to eastern Long Island.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511337e6ff30001d4e6def?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tLegroom wasn't an issue but I had to be sure not to accidentally press the rudder or brake pedals.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51132e7ed0ee001e25d43d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" aircraft is the air conditioning system that provides hot and cold air upon request, just like in a car. It's often required during the summer flying season.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113337ed0ee001e25d445?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe interior is quite loud once the engine starts because it's a small plane so I donned a headset which also allowed me to chat with the pilot during the flight.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511334e6ff30001d4e6de9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIt took less than five minutes to get underway once we shut the doors as the pilot ran through the checklist with airline-like precision.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511331e6ff30001d4e6de3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tBefore we departed, I was also briefed on the SR-20's best safety feature, the onboard parachute. Should anything happen to the pilot, all I'd need to do is bring the throttle and fuel lever back to cut the engine, then pull the parachute.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113317ed0ee001e25d442?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIt would total the plane but we would be alive as we gently floated back down to Earth's surface. Here's where it ejects from.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113357ed0ee001e25d44a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe key perk of using an executive airport is that they're smaller and taxiing to and from the runway takes less time. Case in point, the runway in use for our flight was directly adjacent to the terminal.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511337e6ff30001d4e6df0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tWe departed from Republic Airport on a visual flight plan with Brookhaven Airport, 26 nautical miles to the east.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113377ed0ee001e25d44d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tSitting up front, I had a front-row seat to the action as we took to the skies.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511336e6ff30001d4e6ded?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tWe were airborne within seconds of advancing the throttle. If I was driving on that road below the wing, it would've taken around 40 minutes to get to Brookhaven, so the race was on to see if we could beat that.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113307ed0ee001e25d440?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tSince we weren't operating under an instrument flight plan, the pilot was flying based on visual cues and geography.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511325e6ff30001d4e6dd9?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tWe headed southeast towards the shoreline and followed it all the way to Brookhaven. Our flight barely scratched the surface of the SR-20's capabilities.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51132b7ed0ee001e25d43b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tTwo high definition screens provide advanced navigation systems with other planes showing up on the moving map to help the pilot avoid them.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113317ed0ee001e25d441?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIf we had kept following the shoreline, we could've been in Montauk – 50 miles away – in just under 20 minutes. During the summer, that drive can take hours navigating two-lane roads.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113367ed0ee001e25d44c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tOnce we settled into our cruise, I saw just how unique the Cirrus' design is. Pilots control the aircraft with a side-stick, instead of the normal W-shaped control column...\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51132fe6ff30001d4e6de1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe throttle lever is near-identical to that of an airliner...\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511335e6ff30001d4e6dec?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAnd there are autopilot capabilities.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511336e6ff30001d4e6dee?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAfter flying for about 15 minutes at a top speed of approximately 150 miles per hour, Brookhaven came into view so we turned to the north and prepared to land.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113287ed0ee001e25d439?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tBrookhaven is a popular general aviation airport so we'd have to join the line of Cessnas also landing.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113377ed0ee001e25d44e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIt was nothing the Cirrus couldn't handle thanks to the traffic notifications on the navigation screen.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113357ed0ee001e25d448?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tWe touched down exactly 21 minutes from when we departed Farmingdale, beating the traffic on the road.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51132b7ed0ee001e25d43a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe time savings are more pronounced with longer flights but it was a good showing, considering we had to join the back of a line of planes also wanting to land at Brookhaven.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51132ae6ff30001d4e6ddb?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tOnce we were on the ground, it was time for me to hop in the back.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113327ed0ee001e25d443?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI was expecting it to be like riding in the back of a sedan but it was actually more comfortable and spacious than I imagined.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511332e6ff30001d4e6de6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tMuch like a coupe, the front passenger seat folds down to grant access to the back of the plane.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113337ed0ee001e25d446?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tLegroom was similarly not an issue back here, either.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113387ed0ee001e25d452?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThough, it did help that the front seat was empty.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113397ed0ee001e25d453?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tFor a small piston aircraft, the SR-20 has a deceiving cabin from the outside as it was deeper than I expected just from looking at the plane's exterior.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511339e6ff30001d4e6df2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tJust like on a passenger plane, the SR-20 has USB charging ports, personal reading lamps, and air vents.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113387ed0ee001e25d450?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tA phone can even be connected to the aircraft's speaker system to blast music while flying.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51133e7ed0ee001e25d45f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tTime to see if we could beat our time back to Farmingdale.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51133b7ed0ee001e25d456?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tWe took to the runway one more time and headed back under visual flight rules again.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511338e6ff30001d4e6df1?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tOnce again, we headed down towards the shoreline and followed it back to our origin.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51132ae6ff30001d4e6ddc?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe oversized windows in the back of the SR-20 allowed for some great views along the way.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113387ed0ee001e25d451?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe pilot was talking with air traffic control the entire time we were in the air so we weren't completely on our own.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f511339e6ff30001d4e6df3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe leather seats and air conditioning made the journey quite comfortable.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51133b7ed0ee001e25d458?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tThe Massachusetts islands are popular destinations but some of Hopscotch Air's clients have recently taken the aircraft as far as North Carolina and Chicago on flights over three hours in duration.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5113397ed0ee001e25d454?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAnd I could see why, though undoubtedly slower than the airlines, flying three hours in this plane would have been no different than in a luxury car.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51133c7ed0ee001e25d45c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tSoon enough, Republic Airport came into view and we prepared to land, just 15 minutes after departing Brookhaven.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51133e7ed0ee001e25d45e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tWe just about matched our time on this leg but had managed to fly back and forth in the same amount of time it would've taken to drive one way.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51133ae6ff30001d4e6df5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAfter landing, it was a quick taxi back to the private terminal where our flight ended.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f51133c7ed0ee001e25d45a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Hopscotch Air Air Taxi Cirrus SR-20\" height=\"1875\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Flying on a Hopscotch Air Cirrus SR-20 air taxi.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomas Pallini/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n</div><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a ate":1599401097007},{"createdTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"Anita Hill says she's voting for Joe Biden despite 'the mistakes that he made in the past'","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/anita-hill-says-shes-voting-for-joe-biden-despite-mistakes-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5451ac7ed0ee001e25dbd0?format=jpeg\" alt=\"anita hill\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Anita Hill speaks onstage as Audible presents: &#34;In Love and Struggle&#34; at Audible&#39;s Minetta Lane Theater on February 29, 2020 in New York City.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Craig Barritt/Getty Images for Audible</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Anita Hill told CNN on Saturday she intends to vote for Joe Biden.</li>\n<li>Biden has faced criticism for decades over his handling of the 1991 Senate hearings in which Hill testified that then-Supreme Court nominee Clarence Thomas sexually harassed her.</li>\n<li>Last year, Biden spoke with hill about the 1991 hearings and expressed regret &#8212; a gesture which Hill said at the time was \"not enough.\"</li>\n<li>But Hill told CNN she believed that despite Biden's \"limitations in the past,\" she believed he should be elected in November over President Donald Trump.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>&#160;</p><p>Anita Hill said she intends to vote for Joe Biden in the November election, despite her past criticism of the man who chaired the Senate Judiciary Committee during her testimony against then-Supreme Court nominee Clarence Thomas in 1991.</p><p>Biden spoke with Hill last year and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/joe-biden-regrets-1991-anita-hill-hearings-metoo-movement-2019-3\">expressed regret</a> for the decades-old hearings — a gesture which <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/04/25/us/politics/joe-biden-anita-hill.html\">Hill said at the time was \"not enough.\"</a></p><p>Hill underwent a grueling hearing when she testified that Thomas sexually harassed her when they worked together, and Biden has long been criticized for not providing a fair process for Hill. Thomas, who denied Hill's allegations, was eventually confirmed to the Supreme Court.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/09/05/politics/anita-hill-joe-biden-voting/index.html\">But Hill told CNN on Saturday</a> that despite Biden's shortcomings in the past, she believed he should be elected rather than President Donald Trump.</p><p>\"Notwithstanding all of his limitations in the past, and the mistakes that he made in the past, notwithstanding those — at this point, between Donald Trump and Joe Biden, I think Joe Biden is the person who should be elected in November,\" Hill told CNN.</p><p>\"My commitment is to finding solutions, and I am more than willing to work with him,\" she said, adding that she hoped to work on sexual harassment and gender discrimination issues.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ba2a75080eb351c008b603d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Anita Hill\" height=\"1080\" width=\"1623\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Anita Hill, University of Oklahoma Law Professor, who testified, that she was sexually harassed by Clarence Thomas. 1991 photo.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.apimages.com/metadata/Index/Watchf-AP-A-USA-APHS306262-Anita-Hill/da54b9120e644bb49d8c58cef91af12b/252/0\" target=\"_blank\">AP Photo</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Biden has repeatedly been asked about his conduct during the Hill hearing, and he told CNN in July he \"believed her story from the very beginning\" and wished he \"could have protected her more.\"</p><p>Though Hill was dissatisfied with her conversation with Biden last year, she told CNN she believed he had since shown greater responsibility for his actions.</p><p>\"There was a statement about 'I take accountability; I hold myself responsible for the way the hearing was run,'\" she told CNN. \"And so that, I think, is as close as we've gotten, you know, and that's good. That's an opening.\"</p><p>She continued: \"I want the next president to be somebody that I can go to and talk about the real issues that women, men, and non-binary people are experiencing with violence in this country, that's directed to them because of their gender… I believe that Joe Biden would be that person. I do not believe that Donald Trump would be the person who would hear me.\"</p><ul class=\"read-more-links\"><li>Read more:</li><li><a 22:04:56","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:56","title":"I ate at Golden Corral to see how its 'no touch' all-you-can-eat buffet works and found a COVID-19 src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52ff6f7ed0ee001e25db3d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1333\" width=\"1777\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>\n<p>Golden Corral is one of America&#8217;s most popular buffet chains, known for its bountiful fried chicken and never-ending chocolate fondue fountain.</p>\n</li>\n<li>During COVID-19, restaurants have had to adapt to align with state guidelines.</li>\n<li>I went to a Golden Corral in Iowa assuming it would be a &#8220;no-touch&#8221; buffet. But I was wrong.</li>\n<li>The experience left me feeling uncomfortable about the number of diners and the lack of mitigation efforts.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Under normal circumstances, eating at a Golden Corral can be a fun experience in a gluttonous kind of way.&#160;</p><p>There's an endless array of foods to choose from with unlimited helpings. If you want some orange chicken with a side of mashed potatoes, have at it.</p><p>But the beloved American tradition of all-you-can eat buffets has been severely undercut by the COVID-19 pandemic. Diners across the country have been trying to navigate a new masked world where you're offered hand sanitizer with your glass of water.</p><p>As a chain restaurant lover, I was curious about what eating at a Golden Corral would resemble in the middle of a pandemic.</p><p>After sifting through the restaurant's website, which touts a \"no touch\" buffet and \"enhanced sanitation measures\" I traveled to the nearest location to me at Council Bluffs, Iowa to see what it was like.</p><p>Welcome to the dining journey that I've aptly named \"Covid-Corral.\"</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tWhen I stepped out of my car, the scent of stale grease let me know I made it to my destination.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc707ed0ee001e25db2f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1333\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tPrior to entering the line to pay for my meal, I was greeted by a cautionary banner laying out the rules of Golden Corral during COVID-19.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc78e6ff30001d4e7498?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tDon't move tables, accompany children, and follow the socially-distanced floor markers. However, there was no mention of face masks.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc7ae6ff30001d4e749d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI stood in line and waited for my turn to pay $10.15 for my unlimited breakfast buffet Sunday morning.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc79e6ff30001d4e749b?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIt was then it dawned on me: This wasn't a touchless buffet.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc7be6ff30001d4e749f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIn fact, it was a \"touch everything and act like we're not in the middle of a once-in-a-century pandemic\" buffet.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc78e6ff30001d4e7499?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAs I was choosing my seat in the dining area, there were barely any \"closed\" table signs to encourage social distancing.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI picked a table that was next to the only \"closed\" for social distancing sign that I saw around.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc6fe6ff30001d4e748f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tMy waitress was kind, but she wasn't wearing a face mask. She came by and took my drink order and promptly brought me a diet coke.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc757ed0ee001e25db32?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tI started my COVID-Corral journey by grabbing a plate from a nearby stack that was in the wide open. There were also strange yellow spots I couldn't scrape off.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc6fe6ff30001d4e7490?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tNext, I made my way to everyone's buffet favorite: The salad Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tWhen I sat down I realized I made a weird hodgepodge salad because I was so distracted.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tBut hey, at least my silverware came in an individualized packet.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tAt this point, I definitely had enough.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc7b7ed0ee001e25db39?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden touching tongs, walking around, and sitting in a busy dining room made me feel anxious, even with a face mask on.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc7b7ed0ee001e25db3a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tPrior to the pandemic, Golden Corral's endless array of foods would be my dream. Today, it was my nightmare.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f52fc7ae6ff30001d4e749e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Golden Corral Pandemic Review\" height=\"1500\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Linh Ta/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t\n\tIn Iowa, the only dining restrictions mandate six feet of distance between tables, so technically, the restaurant was up to regulation. Still, it wasn't my ideal dining experience. Turner)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f11b0ccf34d0533b93a99d3?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn47@2020_1/2020/09/06/14-05-33-726_e11e40da148a884b.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f36bd88e89ebf001f044a74?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn63@2020_5/2020/09/06/14-05-29-514_9ac7680377e9fb10.webp","https://i.insider.com/5f4801b9cd2fec00296a4a11?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn59@2020_2/2020/09/06/14-05-48-543_7f0fabf5598ae1b8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn76@2020_4/2020/09/06/14-05-49-381_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=Yuqccco0N34:SPIYsZVUSd0:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn24@2020_4/2020/09/06/14-05-47-400_cf24639e985a4416.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=Yuqccco0N34:SPIYsZVUSd0:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn4@2020_5/2020/09/06/14-05-48-005_51d647a629389bef.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn71@2020_5/2020/09/06/14-05-44-327_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=Yuqccco0N34:SPIYsZVUSd0:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn59@2020_6/2020/09/06/14-05-46-984_32ea5d36c3c1efce.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/Yuqccco0N34":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn67@2020_6/2020/09/06/14-05-27-223_8060a250b659b3cc.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1599401097022},{"createdTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:57","updatedTime":"2020-09-06 22:04:57","title":"7 ways leaders can effectively support employees during the pandemic","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/7-ways-leaders-can-support-employees-during-the-pandemic-2020-9","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f36ba6be89ebf001f044a36?format=jpeg\" alt=\"employee man talking to female boss meeting work office\" height=\"2000\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Effective leaders do these seven things.\n<p class=\"copyright\">EMS-FORSTER-PRODUCTIONS/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>During a pandemic, employees need honest, effective leaders to help them cope with tough times.&#160;</li>\n<li>Heidi Zak, cofounder and CEO of loungewear startup ThirdLove, believes leaders need to be more proactive and create safe spaces for employees to feel seen and supported.&#160;</li>\n<li>You can start to make a difference if you're transparent, agile, and optimistic with your employees. Communicate with them often to share your honest feelings and advocate for them to do the same.</li>\n<li>Establish a company mission, and be willing to adapt and apply it to current events.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p dir=\"ltr\">If 2020 has taught us anything, it's that leadership in today's world requires a wide range of&#160;<a href=\"https://www.inc.com/emma-brudner/the-top-5-soft-skills-of-2020-how-to-develop-them.html\">soft skills</a>.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Employees don't want to work for inauthentic&#160;<a href=\"https://www.inc.com/heidi-zak/the-2-things-you-need-as-a-founder-to-have-a-healthy-relationship-with-your-board-of-directors.html\">founders</a>, executives, or managers. Team members don't feel empowered when working with people who don't have a reasonable level of emotional intelligence. Partners, vendors, and clients don't want to be associated with companies that aren't transparent about the way they do business — and the masses don't want to support companies whose actions don't align with their mission statements.&#160;</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Being an effective leader today, and especially while navigating our \"new normal,\" is about honesty, plain and simple. It means being honest in your day-to-day interactions, honest in the way you do business, and honest about the status of the organization. As many leaders learned back in March (including myself), these are not easy times to navigate — but being open and transparent with your team is crucial to long-term success.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Personally, I believe the coronavirus crisis will change the way people think about leadership forever.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Here's what I think being an effective&#160;<a href=\"https://www.inc.com/magazine/202009/tom-foster/simon-sinek-daymond-john-kendra-scott-business-advice.html?cid=search&_ga=2.91017434.1970114794.1598279515-2120289157.15956026672667\">leader</a>&#160;in our new normal&#160;will look like, moving forward.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">1. Leaders must be proactive in their efforts, and deeply care about how the people around them are doing</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">When you work in an office, you can generally assess when somebody is having a bad day&#160;or if they're upset about something.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Digitally, this becomes much harder. Both at the leadership level as well as the managerial level, we have to be more thoughtful about how we check in on people. This means proactively asking questions like, \"How are you doing these days?\" and actually taking the time to listen.&#160;</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Instead of hopping on a Zoom call and immediately diving into work-related items, take a moment to show you care.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">2. Leaders need to share how they're feeling, as well</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">Transparency in any organization is important.</p><p>But when everyone is working remotely, as difficult as it can be to get a read on how your employees and team members are feeling, it can be even more difficult for them to get a read on how you're doing — since they don't get to see you walking around the office.</p><p>I'm not advocating for oversharing, but especially with your executive team, I do believe it's important to be open and honest about your own feelings as well. I remember back in March, prior to letting people from our company go, I cried while talking to our leadership team. I was really upset, and felt horrible about the decision in front of us. And the other leaders within the company went down that emotional journey with me.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Being an effective leader doesn't mean being emotionless.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">It means having the capacity for the whole range of emotions, and still being able to make sound, logical decisions for the business.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">3. Leaders must create a safe environment where people feel a sense of belonging.</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">One of the questions we ask in our employee surveys is whether they feel that their manager cares about them.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Personally, I believe everyone finds fulfillment in their work only if they believe the people around them care about them as human beings, first. As a leader, it's then your job to create an environment where people feel this sense of belonging, and know that the hours they spend working toward the company's mission mean more than just earning a paycheck.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">4. Leaders have to solidify their mission — and live it out in the world</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">Now more than ever, the mission of a company matters. Customers care about it. Employees care about it. Investors care about it. Everyone wants to know that where they are putting their time, energy, money, and support is behind an organization they believe is impacting the world in some sort of positive way.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Second, and as more and more social impact campaigns shift the world, how your company's mission fits into these larger narratives of humanity can dramatically change the way people see your brand.&#160;</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Your mission, and how it ties into current events, is extremely important.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">5. Leaders must be willing to adapt</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">In a world of uncertainty, adaptability is key. It has always been true that leaders must constantly be thinking 10 steps ahead. But during a global crisis like COVID-19, flexibility and being able to make quick, informed decisions is crucial to keeping the business moving forward.&#160;</p><p dir=\"ltr\">This means making it a regular priority to sit down and run through hypotheticals. \"What would happen to the business if X happened? What would we do if we lost Y? How would we think about the future if we couldn't do Z?\"&#160;</p><p dir=\"ltr\">It's far better to have answers to these types of questions before, rather than during, a difficult time.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">6. Leaders have to remain optimistic about the future, without sugarcoating the present</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">Building a company inherently requires some level of optimism. It's very difficult to build something that doesn't exist yet if you're a pessimist.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">Once a company is off and running, though, the optimism can't stop. Your team needs it. Your co-captains and fellow leaders need it. Everyone around you needs to feel as though they can see the light at the end of the tunnel, just like you can.&#160;</p><p dir=\"ltr\">That said, you also have to guard optimism from delusion. Being optimistic can't mean lying to or deceiving those around you — or especially yourself. Instead, it means being brutally honest, while at the same time acknowledging both the good and the bad, the lessons learned, and the growth to come.</p><h2 dir=\"ltr\">7. Leaders must overcommunicate</h2><p dir=\"ltr\">Right now, especially, every leader should be overcommunicating with their teams.</p><p dir=\"ltr\">On the one hand, this means making sure people are receiving the information they need, when they need it. While working remotely, this might require you to do more frequent check-ins with employees&#160;or to set&#160;reminders to send status updates to key decision makers every day on Slack.&#160;</p><p dir=\"ltr\">On the flipside, though, effective communication also means leaving room for others to speak up. For example, I held an all-hands recently and ended the meeting by asking, \"Does anyone have any questions?\" I let that question hang in the air for 20 or 30 seconds. And it took a while, but eventually someone spoke up and asked a great question. Digitally, creating space for this type of serendipity is crucial — and asks leaders to pause and not be so quick to just end the Zoom meeting and move on to the next thing.</p><div
